FILE 2/22: t_0_market_intelligence_kickoff_and_commissioning_standard.md

# T0 — Market-Intelligence Kickoff & Commissioning Standard

## Document Status
**System:** Market-Intelligence Operating System  
**Layer:** Pre-Analysis Commissioning Layer  
**Designation:** T0  
**Document Type:** Standard  
**Status:** Canonical Draft  
**Purpose Class:** Intake / Scoping / Workflow Initiation / Analysis Readiness

---

## 1. Purpose

The **Market-Intelligence Kickoff & Commissioning Standard** is the formal intake and initiation layer for the Market-Intelligence Operating System.

Its function is to ensure that every ecosystem study begins with sufficient structure, scope definition, decision context, boundary discipline, and evidence expectations before the analytical workflow starts.

This document exists because the operating system can only produce strong conclusions if the input problem is framed correctly. Without a formal kickoff layer, ecosystem studies risk starting with:

- vague ecosystem boundaries
- unclear decision objectives
- missing time horizons
- hidden assumptions
- mismatched evidence expectations
- premature product thinking
- inconsistent output quality across studies

T0 exists to prevent those failures by standardizing how the system is commissioned.

---

## 2. Strategic Role in the Operating System

The Market-Intelligence Operating System already contains:

- the foundational ecosystem analysis doctrine
- the intelligence suite
- the strategy suite
- the T1–T19 standalone standards

What it still needs is a formal front door.

T0 serves ten strategic roles:

1. **Commissioning discipline** — ensures every analysis begins from a defined brief rather than a loose prompt.
2. **Boundary control** — defines what ecosystem is actually being studied and what is excluded.
3. **Decision alignment** — forces clarity on what decision the analysis is meant to support.
4. **Input sufficiency** — ensures the system has enough context to generate meaningful conclusions.
5. **Workflow routing** — determines which documents in the operating system are required versus conditional for a given study.
6. **Evidence readiness** — clarifies expected source classes, available evidence, and known information gaps before analysis begins.
7. **Anti-drift protection** — prevents premature collapse into product ideation, features, or tactical execution.
8. **Comparability support** — makes multiple ecosystem studies easier to compare later under T18.
9. **Agent readiness** — creates a standardized template that humans or agents can fill consistently.
10. **Quality gating** — establishes whether the study is ready to begin or whether more scoping is needed first.

T0 is therefore the formal commissioning layer for the full operating system.

---

## 3. What This Document Is

This document is:

- the official kickoff and intake standard for the operating system
- a commissioning brief template
- a readiness gate before Ecosystem Analysis begins
- a workflow-routing standard that determines which downstream documents should be produced
- the canonical starting point for each new ecosystem study

---

## 4. What This Document Is Not

The Kickoff & Commissioning Standard is **not**:

- the Ecosystem Analysis itself
- a product brief
- a feature ideation document
- a market-size memo
- a general brainstorm worksheet
- a substitute for T11 evidence governance or T12 uncertainty governance

It is the structured setup layer that enables all later documents to be produced with rigor.

---

## 5. Core Recommendation

Yes — the operating system should have a formal kickoff template standard.

Without T0, each ecosystem study must be improvised at the point of entry. That weakens consistency, increases analytical drift, and makes it harder to know whether conclusions are strong because the system worked or weak because the study began with poor framing.

With T0, every ecosystem analysis starts from:

- a defined ecosystem specification
- a clear decision question
- declared boundaries
- known evidence conditions
- a document-routing plan
- explicit readiness criteria

This should be treated as mandatory for all formal studies.

---

## 6. Position in the Full Workflow

T0 sits before all other documents.

### Full operating sequence
1. **T0 — Kickoff & Commissioning Standard**
2. **Ecosystem Analysis Standard**
3. **T1–T5 Intelligence Layer**
4. **T6–T10 Strategy Layer**
5. **T11–T19 Companion Governance / Conversion / Portfolio / Learning Layer**

T0 does not replace any existing document. It governs when and how the rest of the system begins.

---

## 7. When to Use T0

T0 should be used whenever:

- a new ecosystem is being introduced into the system
- a new platform ecosystem, market ecosystem, or vertical is being studied
- a prior ecosystem study is being substantially reframed
- an agent or researcher needs a standardized intake packet before analysis begins
- multiple ecosystems will later be compared, prioritized, or routed into the same operating system

T0 should be completed before the Ecosystem Analysis is started.

---

## 8. Outputs of T0

A completed T0 should produce the following outputs:

- a clear ecosystem specification
- a clearly stated governing decision question
- a scope boundary definition
- a declared time horizon
- a known-input inventory
- a known-gap inventory
- a routing decision for which downstream documents are mandatory, recommended, or optional
- a readiness judgment on whether the study can begin immediately
- a canonical kickoff packet that can be handed to a researcher or agent

---

## 9. T0 Governing Questions

A good kickoff process should answer the following before analysis begins:

1. What ecosystem exactly are we studying?
2. What decision is this study meant to support?
3. What is inside scope and outside scope?
4. What geography, platform, segment, or category boundaries apply?
5. What time horizon matters?
6. What inputs do we already have?
7. What information is missing but important?
8. Which downstream documents are required for this case?
9. What would make the study insufficient before it even begins?
10. What must remain explicitly out of bounds to avoid premature ideation?

---

## 10. Required Structure of the Standard

Every T0 commissioning packet should contain the following sections.

### 10.1 Section 1 — Analysis Request Header
This section defines the basic request metadata.

Required fields:
- study title
- ecosystem name
- commissioning date
- requested by
- owner / analyst / agent
- status
- version

### 10.2 Section 2 — Governing Decision Question
This section states the exact decision the study is meant to support.

Examples:
- Is this ecosystem strategically worth entering?
- What is the best entry path into this ecosystem?
- Is this platform ecosystem viable for a small independent developer?
- Which of several ecosystems should receive focus first?

This must be specific. A vague request produces vague analysis.

### 10.3 Section 3 — Ecosystem Specification
This section defines what the ecosystem is.

Required fields:
- ecosystem type
- primary domain
- core market or platform name
- key participant groups
- primary interfaces or surfaces
- primary channels or marketplaces
- relevant business model context
- one-paragraph ecosystem description

This section should describe the ecosystem itself, not a proposed product idea.

### 10.4 Section 4 — Scope Boundaries
This section defines what is inside and outside the study.

Required fields:
- geographic scope
- customer / participant scope
- platform scope
- adjacent categories included
- adjacent categories excluded
- timeframe of interest
- explicit exclusions

This section is critical for preventing analysis sprawl.

### 10.5 Section 5 — Decision Horizon and Strategic Context
This section defines the temporal and strategic lens of the study.

Required fields:
- decision horizon
- urgency level
- why this study matters now
- strategic objective supported
- level of rigor required

The same ecosystem may be studied differently depending on whether the goal is quick-profit exploration, long-term strategic positioning, or platform portfolio comparison.

### 10.6 Section 6 — Known Inputs and Existing Evidence
This section records what is already known before research begins.

Required fields:
- documents already available
- prior ecosystem knowledge
- existing audits, notes, or prior analyses
- connected platform or marketplace knowledge
- known players or actors already identified
- known relevant policies or constraints

This prevents the system from ignoring available context.

### 10.7 Section 7 — Known Unknowns and Open Questions
This section identifies what is already suspected to be unclear.

Required fields:
- top open questions
- areas of likely ambiguity
- terms needing clarification
- likely evidence gaps
- risk areas that may require special attention

This section does not replace T12. It is pre-analysis uncertainty framing.

### 10.8 Section 8 — Workflow Routing Matrix
This section determines which downstream documents should be produced.

Required outputs:
- Ecosystem Analysis Standard: mandatory or not
- T1–T5: mandatory / recommended / optional
- T6–T10: mandatory / recommended / optional
- T11–T19: mandatory / recommended / optional

Routing should be justified briefly.

### 10.9 Section 9 — Readiness Check
This section determines whether the analysis can begin.

Possible statuses:
- ready to begin
- ready with cautions
- not ready — more scoping required
- blocked — critical information missing

### 10.10 Section 10 — Anti-Drift Constraints
This section explicitly states what the study must not do prematurely.

Examples:
- do not propose products yet
- do not recommend features yet
- do not collapse into pricing or go-to-market tactics yet
- do not assume the ecosystem is attractive before analysis proves it

This keeps the operating system disciplined.

---

## 11. Workflow Routing Logic

T0 should include a routing framework that determines which downstream documents are needed for the specific study.

### 11.1 Always mandatory
For formal ecosystem studies, the following should generally be mandatory:
- Ecosystem Analysis Standard
- T10 Entry Vector Analysis, if the study is meant to support actual strategic entry

### 11.2 Usually mandatory for serious studies
These are generally required unless the ecosystem is unusually simple:
- T1 Culture Map
- T2 Lever Architecture
- T3 Participant Decision Architecture
- T5 Competitive Topology
- T6 Trust Architecture
- T8 Risk & Fragility Map
- T9 Capital Flow Atlas

### 11.3 Conditional based on ecosystem shape
These may be mandatory depending on context:
- T4 Language & Semiotics Map when communication fit matters materially
- T7 Temporal Rhythm Map when timing or seasonality matters materially
- T17 Platform Access & Constraint Audit when platform dependence is material
- T18 Portfolio Scorecard when multiple ecosystems or pathways will be compared

### 11.4 Mandatory when conversion and governance begin
These become required once the study is moving beyond pure analysis:
- T11 Evidence Ledger
- T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register
- T13 Executive Decision Memo
- T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief
- T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard
- T16 Refresh & Monitoring Protocol
- T19 Learning Capture Memo

---

## 12. Minimum Required Inputs Before Starting

A study should not begin formally unless T0 can answer, at minimum:

- what ecosystem is being analyzed
- what decision the study supports
- what is inside scope
- what is outside scope
- what time horizon matters
- what the strategic objective is
- what is already known
- what is obviously missing

If those cannot be answered, the study is not ready.

---

## 13. Readiness Criteria

A study is **ready to begin** only if all of the following are true:

1. The ecosystem is defined clearly enough to distinguish it from adjacent spaces.
2. The governing decision question is explicit.
3. Scope boundaries are set.
4. Time horizon is stated.
5. Strategic objective is stated.
6. Known inputs are logged.
7. Known unknowns are acknowledged.
8. Routing decisions for downstream documents are made.
9. Anti-drift constraints are defined.

If these conditions are not met, the study should not advance into the Ecosystem Analysis Standard.

---

## 14. Required Usage Rules

The following rules are mandatory.

### Rule 1 — No analysis without a governing decision question
The system should not begin formal work on a vague ecosystem prompt.

### Rule 2 — No product ideation in T0
T0 is for scoping the ecosystem study, not proposing products.

### Rule 3 — No scope ambiguity
Inside-scope and outside-scope boundaries must be stated explicitly.

### Rule 4 — No hidden assumptions about why the ecosystem matters
The strategic objective and urgency must be stated directly.

### Rule 5 — No skipping routing
T0 must determine which downstream documents are required.

### Rule 6 — No starting with zero evidence awareness
Known inputs and known gaps must be logged before beginning.

### Rule 7 — No false readiness
If key scoping elements are missing, T0 must say the study is not ready.

---

## 15. Recommended Operating Procedure

### Step 1 — Define the ecosystem
State exactly what market, platform, or ecosystem is being studied.

### Step 2 — Define the decision
State exactly what decision the analysis must support.

### Step 3 — Draw the boundaries
Clarify geography, participants, platforms, time horizon, and exclusions.

### Step 4 — Log what is already known
Capture existing documents, known actors, existing platform knowledge, and prior findings.

### Step 5 — Log what is not known
Identify the major open questions and likely gaps.

### Step 6 — Route the workflow
Decide which of the Ecosystem Analysis, T1–T10, and T11–T19 documents will be required.

### Step 7 — Run the readiness check
Determine whether the study can begin now or needs more scoping first.

### Step 8 — Launch the analysis
Only after T0 is complete should the operating system proceed into Ecosystem Analysis.

---

## 16. Quality Standard / Acceptance Criteria

The Kickoff & Commissioning Standard should be considered acceptable only if all of the following are true:

1. The ecosystem is clearly specified.
2. The governing decision question is explicit.
3. Scope boundaries are defined.
4. Strategic objective and time horizon are defined.
5. Known inputs are logged.
6. Known unknowns are logged.
7. Workflow routing is completed.
8. Readiness status is explicit.
9. Anti-drift constraints are explicit.
10. The packet is clear enough that a new analyst or agent could begin the study without improvising the foundation.

---

## 17. Failure Modes and Misuse Warnings

Common failure modes include:

### 17.1 Vague ecosystem naming
Labeling the ecosystem too broadly or too narrowly to support useful analysis.

### 17.2 Decision ambiguity
Starting a study without knowing what decision the study is meant to inform.

### 17.3 Product contamination
Allowing the kickoff template to smuggle in preferred product directions before analysis.

### 17.4 Missing routing discipline
Failing to determine which downstream documents are required for the case.

### 17.5 Scope sprawl
Not defining what is excluded, leading to endless adjacent-market drift.

### 17.6 False readiness
Starting formal analysis even though key context is missing.

### 17.7 Agent inconsistency
Using freeform prompts instead of a standard intake packet, causing uneven quality across ecosystem studies.

---

## 19. Recommended Naming Convention

Recommended canonical file name:

`T0_Market_Intelligence_Kickoff_and_Commissioning_Standard.md`

Recommended per-study intake artifact naming:

`<ecosystem_name>_T0_Commissioning_Packet.md`

---

## 20. Relationship to Agentic Research Systems

T0 should be the standard packet used whenever an agent is instructed to begin a new ecosystem study.

This means:

- the fields should be explicit and machine-legible where possible
- the routing matrix should make downstream document selection deterministic
- readiness status should be explicit rather than implied
- anti-drift constraints should be visible so agents do not jump prematurely into ideation

An agent should not begin a formal ecosystem study without a completed or near-complete T0 packet.

---

## 21. Versioning Notes

The Kickoff & Commissioning Standard should evolve when any of the following occur:

- repeated studies fail because of poor scoping rather than poor analysis
- routing logic proves too vague or too rigid
- analysts or agents repeatedly begin work without sufficient inputs
- portfolio comparison reveals inconsistent study setup quality
- T19 learning shows that early framing errors repeatedly distort later conclusions

Version updates should record what commissioning weakness prompted the revision.

---

## 22. Final Standard Statement

A rigorous analysis system needs a rigorous beginning.

The Market-Intelligence Kickoff & Commissioning Standard exists to ensure that every ecosystem study begins with the necessary clarity, boundaries, evidence awareness, and workflow routing to support strong downstream conclusions.

Without T0, the operating system depends on improvisation at the point of entry.
With T0, it begins from discipline.

FILE 3/22: t_10_entry_vector_analysis_standard.md
================================================================================

# T10 — Entry Vector Analysis Standard

## Document Status
**System:** Market-Intelligence Operating System  
**Layer:** Strategy Layer  
**Designation:** T10  
**Document Type:** Standard  
**Status:** Canonical Draft  
**Purpose Class:** Strategic Entry Design / Vector Ranking / Market Insertion Analysis

---

## 1. Purpose

The **Entry Vector Analysis** is the authoritative strategic-entry artifact for the Market-Intelligence Operating System.

Its function is to translate the full analytical stack into ranked, decision-grade pathways for entering an ecosystem.

This document exists because the operating system is not meant to stop at description. After terrain, intelligence, trust, timing, risk, and economic structure have been mapped, the organization still needs to answer the central strategic question:

**Where should we enter, through what path, and why that path instead of another?**

T10 exists to answer that question without collapsing prematurely into product design, implementation planning, or tactical execution. It converts the full stack into structured entry logic.

---

## 2. Strategic Role in the Operating System

T10 is the capstone of the original market-intelligence stack.

The Ecosystem Analysis defines the terrain. T1–T5 deepen ecosystem intelligence. T6–T9 add strategic structure around trust, timing, fragility, and capital flow. T10 synthesizes all of that into ranked entry vectors.

T10 serves ten strategic roles:

1. **Synthesis** — converts the full stack into decision-grade entry logic.
2. **Pathway design** — identifies the specific surfaces, segments, channels, or wedges through which entry may succeed.
3. **Vector ranking** — compares alternative pathways rather than assuming one obvious route exists.
4. **Constraint integration** — carries forward trust, timing, fragility, capital, and platform realities.
5. **False-opportunity filtration** — prevents elegant but non-viable entry ideas from advancing.
6. **Strategic sequencing** — clarifies whether a broad push, narrow wedge, partnership route, platform-native route, or adjacent route makes the most sense.
7. **Handoff discipline** — creates the final upstream artifact before conversion into T13, T14, and T15.
8. **Portfolio readiness** — provides comparable opportunity pathways that can later be assessed under T18.
9. **Validation focus** — reveals which pathway-specific assumptions must be tested first.
10. **Decision accountability** — records why one entry path outranked others at this moment.

T10 is therefore the operating system’s primary strategic-entry synthesis layer.

---

## 3. What This Document Is

This document is:

- a ranked analysis of strategic entry pathways
- a synthesis document built from the full operating-system stack
- a pre-concept strategic decision artifact
- a bridge from ecosystem intelligence into actionable opportunity selection

---

## 4. What This Document Is Not

The Entry Vector Analysis is **not**:

- a product brief
- a PRD
- a launch plan
- a marketing campaign plan
- a feature roadmap
- a sales playbook
- a loose brainstorm of possible ideas

It should not prescribe implementation details, specific build scopes, or execution tasks. Its job is to identify and rank entry paths, not to operationalize them.

---

## 5. When to Commission or Use It

T10 should be commissioned only after the analytical foundation is mature enough to support real strategic choice.

It becomes mandatory whenever any of the following are true:

- the organization needs to decide where to enter an ecosystem
- multiple plausible pathways, segments, or interfaces exist
- concept work is about to begin and must be constrained by upstream strategy
- portfolio prioritization will require a clean statement of each opportunity’s best entry path
- the team risks drifting from analysis into ad hoc ideation without a disciplined bridge

T10 should not be produced too early. A weak T10 is usually a symptom of unfinished upstream work.

---

## 6. Mandatory vs Conditional Use

**Mandatory** for:

- any market-intelligence effort intended to lead to actual opportunity selection
- any ecosystem with more than one plausible entry path
- any effort that will proceed into T13, T14, T15, T17, or T18
- any strategic process where the mode of entry matters as much as the existence of demand

**Conditionally recommended** for:

- one-off descriptive research that will not inform real strategic choice
- very immature ecosystem scans where no credible pathway analysis can yet be supported

Where the goal is to move from understanding a market to entering it, T10 should be treated as required.

---

## 7. Inputs Required

The Entry Vector Analysis requires the following inputs:

### 7.1 Foundational Inputs
- Ecosystem Analysis
- T1 Culture Map
- T2 Lever Architecture
- T3 Participant Decision Architecture
- T4 Language & Semiotics Map
- T5 Competitive Topology
- T6 Trust Architecture
- T7 Temporal Rhythm Map
- T8 Risk & Fragility Map
- T9 Capital Flow Atlas

### 7.2 Governance Inputs
- T11 Evidence Ledger where available
- T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register where available
- evidence quality, freshness, and contradiction status from the operating system

### 7.3 Strategic Inputs
- decision horizon
- resource constraints
- risk tolerance
- portfolio context where relevant

---

## 8. Outputs Produced

T10 produces the following outputs:

- a set of clearly defined entry vectors
- ranked comparison of those vectors
- rationale for why the leading vectors outrank the others
- vector-specific assumptions, constraints, and no-go conditions
- clear handoff material for T13, T14, and T15

These outputs are the final pre-concept strategic products of the original stack.

---

## 9. Position in Sequencing Logic

T10 is the last document in the original ten-document system.

Recommended sequence:

1. Ecosystem Analysis completed
2. T1–T9 completed or sufficiently mature
3. **T10 Entry Vector Analysis produced**
4. T13 Executive Decision Memo may then compress the selected or ranked vector set
5. T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief may then translate a selected vector into bounded concept candidates
6. T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard may then define how the key assumptions behind the chosen vector or derived concept should be tested

T10 is the bridge between analysis and strategic commitment.

---

## 10. Relationship to Other Documents

### Upstream Relationships
T10 depends on the full analytical stack.

In particular:

- **Ecosystem Analysis** defines the ecosystem terrain and structural opportunity surface
- **T1** clarifies cultural fit and symbolic alignment risk
- **T2** reveals leverage points and movement mechanics
- **T3** reveals participant-specific decision pathways
- **T4** clarifies communication fit and language-native entry requirements
- **T5** defines the competitive field and real whitespace
- **T6** clarifies credibility and legitimacy requirements
- **T7** reveals timing windows and lag structure
- **T8** exposes fragility and breakage paths
- **T9** defines economic access, payer logic, and value capture structure

### Downstream Relationships
T10 directly supports:

- **T13 Executive Decision Memo** by providing ranked vector options and their strategic logic
- **T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief** by supplying the vector selected for concept translation
- **T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard** by identifying vector-specific assumptions that require testing
- **T17 Platform Access & Constraint Audit** when one or more vectors depend materially on platform-mediated entry
- **T18 Cross-Ecosystem Portfolio Scorecard** by providing comparable entry-path logic across opportunities
- **T19 Learning Capture Memo** by preserving what entry logic was chosen and why

---

## 11. Core Analytical Questions

T10 should allow a reviewer to answer the following questions quickly:

1. What are the plausible ways to enter this ecosystem?
2. Which vectors are most credible, usable, and economically meaningful?
3. Which vectors fail because of trust, timing, fragility, or economic access?
4. Which participant, segment, interface, or channel should the organization enter through first?
5. Where is the narrowest viable wedge?
6. Where is the strongest leverage-adjusted path?
7. Which vectors are strategically elegant but practically weak?
8. Which vectors require platform access, partnerships, or trust transfer to work?
9. What assumptions most threaten each vector?
10. Which vector should receive further conversion and validation attention first?

---

## 12. Required Structure of the Document

Every Entry Vector Analysis must contain the following eight sections.

### 12.1 Section 1 — Vector Universe
**Governing question:** What are the full set of plausible entry vectors available in this ecosystem?

This section must identify the complete first-pass set of serious entry vectors before ranking narrows the field.

Vector types may include:

- segment-first entry
- workflow-first entry
- platform-native entry
- platform-adjacent entry
- trust-transfer entry
- partnership-led entry
- compliance-led entry
- economic-wedge entry
- timing-window entry
- adjacent-surface entry

Vectors should be framed as structured entry pathways, not product ideas.

### 12.2 Section 2 — Vector Definition Profiles
**Governing question:** What exactly is each vector, and how does it work?

Each serious vector must receive a concise profile including:

- vector name
- entry surface
- primary participant or segment targeted
- core leverage logic
- trust basis
- timing basis
- economic basis
- primary constraints

### 12.3 Section 3 — Comparative Evaluation
**Governing question:** How do the vectors compare against one another on the dimensions that actually matter?

This section must compare vectors across at least the following dimensions:

- strategic attractiveness
- trust feasibility
- timing fit
- fragility burden
- economic access / capital capture quality
- competitive openness
- validation burden
- resource fit

The comparison may be qualitative, scored, or hybrid, but it must be structured and explicit.

### 12.4 Section 4 — Ranked Vector Set
**Governing question:** Which vectors outrank the others, and in what order?

This section must produce an ordered ranking of the viable vectors.

For each ranked vector, document:

- overall position
- why it outranks the next-best alternative
- what would have to change for the ranking to change

### 12.5 Section 5 — Vector-Specific Assumptions and Constraints
**Governing question:** What must be true for each vector to work, and what constrains it?

This section must identify for each serious vector:

- major assumptions
- hard constraints
- credibility requirements
- platform or partner dependencies
- timing dependencies
- economic dependencies

### 12.6 Section 6 — Rejected or Deprioritized Vectors
**Governing question:** Which vectors were considered but ranked lower, and why?

This section must identify vectors that were rejected or deprioritized and state clearly why.

Examples include:

- too fragile
- too crowded
- too slow
- too dependent on trust transfer that is not available
- too weak economically
- too platform-constrained
- too resource-intensive relative to alternatives

### 12.7 Section 7 — Strategic Entry Implications
**Governing question:** What does the ranked vector set imply for the next strategic move?

This section must remain analytical.

It should identify:

- which vector appears most promising now
- whether a narrow wedge or broader entry frame is structurally wiser
- whether sequencing matters, such as starting with one vector and expanding later
- where the organization should remain cautious before committing downstream work

### 12.8 Section 8 — Handoff Guidance
**Governing question:** What should flow next into T13, T14, and T15?

This section must identify:

- which vector should move into T13 compression first
- which vector, if any, should move into T14 conversion
- which assumptions should be elevated into T15 validation priority
- whether additional T17 platform work is required before concept conversion

---

## 13. Required Data Fields

At minimum, every T10 document should include the following fields.

### 13.1 Header Fields
- **Document ID**
- **Ecosystem name**
- **Version**
- **Date**
- **Prepared by**
- **Source Ecosystem Analysis ID**
- **Status**

### 13.2 Vector Definition Fields
- **Vector name**
- **Vector type**
- **Entry surface**
- **Primary participant / segment**
- **Core leverage logic**
- **Trust basis**
- **Timing basis**
- **Economic basis**
- **Primary constraints**

### 13.3 Comparative Evaluation Fields
- **Vector name**
- **Strategic attractiveness**
- **Trust feasibility**
- **Timing fit**
- **Fragility burden**
- **Economic access quality**
- **Competitive openness**
- **Validation burden**
- **Resource fit**
- **Comparative note**

### 13.4 Ranking Fields
- **Rank**
- **Vector name**
- **Why it outranks the next alternative**
- **Ranking reversal condition**

### 13.5 Assumption and Constraint Fields
- **Vector name**
- **Assumption**
- **Constraint type**
- **Severity**
- **Why it matters**

### 13.6 Rejection Fields
- **Rejected / deprioritized vector**
- **Reason for lower ranking**
- **Could it become viable later?**
- **What would need to change?**

### 13.7 Handoff Fields
- **Selected vector for T13**
- **Selected vector for T14**
- **Priority assumptions for T15**
- **Need for T17?**
- **Next action note**

---

## 14. Vector Universe Standard

This section must cast a wide but disciplined net before narrowing.

The purpose is to avoid premature fixation on one elegant path. The vector universe should include all plausible serious modes of entry supported by the upstream analysis.

Vectors should be framed around **how entry happens**, not what product gets built.

Examples:

- entering through a neglected participant segment
- entering through a workflow chokepoint
- entering through a platform marketplace
- entering through a partner or trust-transfer route
- entering through a timing window or compliance moment

---

## 15. Vector Definition Profiles Standard

Each vector profile must be precise enough to compare, but not so detailed that it becomes an implementation plan.

A good vector profile should make clear:

- where the entry starts
- who it addresses first
- why that point of entry has leverage
- what trust, timing, and economic logic support it
- what constraints immediately shape it

The profile should be strong enough that two analysts could distinguish it clearly from adjacent vectors.

---

## 16. Comparative Evaluation Standard

This section must be structured, not rhetorical.

At minimum, each vector must be compared across the following dimensions:

- **Strategic attractiveness** — overall quality of the opportunity surface the vector accesses
- **Trust feasibility** — how credible the entry path is likely to be
- **Timing fit** — how aligned the vector is with current ecosystem rhythm
- **Fragility burden** — how brittle the vector is under T8 logic
- **Economic access quality** — whether the vector reaches spend and capture credibly
- **Competitive openness** — whether the vector enters through overcrowded or open terrain
- **Validation burden** — how much must be proven before advancing confidently
- **Resource fit** — whether the vector matches the organization’s actual capabilities and bandwidth

The comparative structure may use numerical scoring, qualitative bands, or both, but the basis of comparison must be visible.

---

## 17. Ranked Vector Set Standard

This section must produce a genuine ordering, not a vague set of options.

The ranking should make clear:

- which vector is first priority
- which vector is second-best and why
- whether any vector is worth parallel attention
- whether some vectors should be monitored rather than advanced

The top-ranked vector should not be declared “best” without showing why it outranks the alternatives under the criteria chosen.

---

## 18. Vector-Specific Assumptions and Constraints Standard

This section must keep the ranking honest.

For each serious vector, it should identify:

- what must be true for the vector to work
- what trust, timing, economic, platform, or fragility constraints limit it
- which assumptions are soft and which are hard gating conditions

This section should connect naturally to T12 and T15 when those documents are used downstream.

---

## 19. Rejected or Deprioritized Vectors Standard

This section must preserve negative strategic learning.

Lower-ranked vectors should not simply disappear. Each should have a stated reason for its lower position, such as:

- excessive fragility
- poor timing fit
- weak economic access
- low trust feasibility
- platform constraints
- poor resource fit
- low competitive openness

This section prevents the system from repeatedly reconsidering weak vectors without remembering why they were deprioritized.

---

## 20. Strategic Entry Implications Standard

This section must remain analytical.

It should identify:

- whether the ecosystem appears to reward narrow wedge entry or broader entry
- whether trust or timing argues for sequencing rather than immediate scale
- whether the leading vector requires concept restraint because of fragility or credibility limits
- whether the second-ranked vector should remain in reserve or active monitoring

It should not prescribe execution tasks or build requirements in detail.

---

## 21. Handoff Guidance Standard

This section is the formal bridge out of the original stack.

It must identify:

- which ranked vector should be compressed into T13 first
- which vector should become the source vector for T14 if concept conversion proceeds
- which assumptions should enter T15 as high-priority validation items
- whether additional T17 platform analysis is needed before downstream conversion

This section is what turns T10 from a terminal report into a usable system handoff.

---

## 22. Research Methodology Standard

The Entry Vector Analysis should follow a synthesis-and-ranking methodology.

Recommended minimum protocol:

### 22.1 Candidate Vector Generation
Generate the plausible entry vectors based on upstream documents rather than ideation alone.

### 22.2 Constraint Integration
Carry forward trust, timing, fragility, competitive, and capital constraints into each vector profile.

### 22.3 Comparative Evaluation
Assess vectors against explicit criteria rather than intuitive preference.

### 22.4 Rank Formation
Produce an ordered vector set with reversal conditions.

### 22.5 Handoff Preparation
Identify what should proceed into T13, T14, T15, and T17.

The methodology should prioritize disciplined synthesis over creativity detached from evidence.

---

## 23. Source and Evidence Expectations

T10 must remain anchored in the upstream analytical stack.

Source expectations:

- every serious vector should be traceable to specific upstream insights
- vector ranking should not rely on intuition alone
- comparative judgments should distinguish strong evidence from interpretive synthesis
- weakly supported vectors may be included, but should be marked provisional
- contradictions or freshness risks in the upstream documents should be carried into ranking logic where material

T10 is synthesis-heavy, but it must still be evidence-governed.

---

## 24. Length Calibration

Recommended target length: **3,500–5,500 words**.  
Maximum: **7,000 words**.

If the document materially exceeds the maximum, it may be cataloguing too many low-quality vectors or repeating upstream analysis rather than synthesizing it.

---

## 25. Required Usage Rules

The following rules are mandatory.

### Rule 1 — No product drift
T10 must define entry pathways, not product concepts or feature plans.

### Rule 2 — No vector invention detached from the stack
Every serious vector must be grounded in upstream analysis.

### Rule 3 — No hidden comparison logic
The basis for ranking must be explicit.

### Rule 4 — No single-vector tunnel vision
A real vector universe must be considered before ranking narrows the field.

### Rule 5 — No trust, timing, fragility, or economic blind spots
Those constraints must be integrated directly into evaluation.

### Rule 6 — No quiet deletion of weak vectors
Rejected or deprioritized vectors must be recorded and explained.

### Rule 7 — No terminal dead end
T10 must provide handoff guidance into T13, T14, T15, and T17 where relevant.

---

## 26. Recommended Operating Procedure

### Step 1 — Confirm upstream maturity
Ensure the Ecosystem Analysis and T1–T9 are sufficiently mature to support synthesis.

### Step 2 — Generate the vector universe
Identify all serious entry paths supported by the evidence.

### Step 3 — Define each vector precisely
Create concise profiles with entry surface, leverage, trust, timing, economics, and constraints.

### Step 4 — Compare vectors systematically
Evaluate them using explicit dimensions and comparable logic.

### Step 5 — Rank the vectors
Produce an ordered set with clear rationale and reversal conditions.

### Step 6 — Surface assumptions and rejected paths
Keep the ranking honest and preserve negative learning.

### Step 7 — Prepare the handoff
Identify what should move into T13, T14, T15, and T17 next.

---

## 27. Quality Standard / Acceptance Criteria

The Entry Vector Analysis should be considered acceptable only if all of the following are true:

1. The vector universe includes all serious plausible paths.
2. Each vector is defined clearly and consistently.
3. Comparative evaluation criteria are explicit.
4. Trust, timing, fragility, economic access, and resource fit are integrated directly into comparison.
5. The ranked vector set is clear and justified.
6. Lower-ranked vectors are recorded and explained.
7. Vector-specific assumptions and constraints are visible.
8. Strategic implications remain analytical rather than tactical.
9. Handoff guidance into downstream documents is explicit.
10. The document provides a disciplined bridge from analysis into strategic commitment.

---

## 28. Failure Modes and Misuse Warnings

Common failure modes include:

### 28.1 Ideation leakage
Confusing entry vectors with product ideas or features.

### 28.2 Elegant-vector bias
Overrating strategically beautiful vectors that fail on trust, timing, or economic access.

### 28.3 Hidden ranking logic
Presenting a preferred vector without showing the comparative basis.

### 28.4 Premature narrowing
Ignoring plausible vectors because of early attachment to one path.

### 28.5 Constraint amnesia
Failing to carry forward fragility, trust, platform, or capital limits from the upstream documents.

### 28.6 No rejection memory
Dropping weak vectors without recording why they lost.

### 28.7 Dead-end synthesis
Producing a strong ranking that does not clearly feed T13, T14, or T15.

---

## 29. Minimum Template

The following structure should be included in implementation.

## 29.1 Entry Vector Analysis Template

### Header
- Document ID
- Ecosystem Name
- Version
- Date
- Prepared By
- Source Ecosystem Analysis ID
- Status

### 1. Vector Universe
| Vector Name | Vector Type | Entry Surface | Primary Participant / Segment | Core Logic |
|---|---|---|---|---|

|---|---|---|---|---|

| Vector Name | Strategic Attractiveness | Trust Feasibility | Timing Fit | Fragility Burden | Economic Access Quality | Competitive Openness | Validation Burden | Resource Fit | Comparative Note |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

| Rank | Vector Name | Why It Outranks the Next Alternative | Ranking Reversal Condition |

|---|---|---|---|---|

### 9. Supporting References
- Ecosystem Analysis
- T1–T9
- T11 if available
- T12 if available

---

## 30. Relationship to Agentic Research Systems

The Entry Vector Analysis should be structured so that agents can assist with synthesis and comparison without collapsing strategic judgment into automated ranking.

This means:

- vectors should be discrete and stable units
- comparative criteria should be explicit
- ranking rationale should remain reviewable
- assumptions and constraints should remain visible alongside rank
- downstream handoff fields should be machine-legible and human-auditable

An agent may help assemble candidate vectors and organize comparisons.
The operating system must still judge which entry path is strategically best.

---

## 31. Versioning Notes

The Entry Vector Analysis Standard should evolve when any of the following occur:

- repeated use shows missing vector categories or comparison dimensions
- T13 and T14 repeatedly reveal that T10 vectors are arriving too vague or too broad
- T15 validation shows that ranking logic is underweighting key assumptions
- T17 platform analysis reveals stronger platform-path dependence than currently modeled
- T18 portfolio comparison requires tighter normalization of vector quality across ecosystems
- T19 learning shows that selected vectors repeatedly fail for reasons the current structure did not surface early enough

Version updates should record what entry-synthesis weakness prompted the revision.

---

## 32. Final Standard Statement

Understanding an ecosystem is not enough. The system must also determine how to enter it.

The Entry Vector Analysis exists to turn the full analytical stack into ranked strategic pathways that can be judged, compared, and handed off into decision, concept conversion, and validation.

Without T10, the operating system can produce rich understanding.
With T10, it can produce a direction.

---

For practical use, the Entry Vector Analysis may be maintained in:

The format may vary.
The entry-synthesis discipline may not.


================================================================================
FILE 4/22: t_11_evidence_ledger_standard.md

# T11 — Evidence Ledger Standard

## Document Status
**System:** Market-Intelligence Operating System  
**Layer:** Companion Governance Layer  
**Designation:** T11  
**Document Type:** Standard  
**Status:** Canonical Draft  
**Purpose Class:** Traceability / Evidence Governance / Audit Control

---

## 1. Purpose

The **Evidence Ledger** is the authoritative evidence-governance artifact for the Market-Intelligence Operating System.

Its function is to create a single, structured record of the sources, claims, confidence boundaries, contradictions, and freshness conditions that support all downstream analytical work.

The ledger exists to ensure that the operating system does not merely produce compelling analysis, but produces analysis that can be:

- traced
- challenged
- refreshed
- defended
- revised
- compared over time

The Evidence Ledger is the system’s control layer for factual grounding.

---

## 2. Strategic Role in the Operating System

The Market-Intelligence Operating System already produces analytical outputs that depend on disciplined sourcing, confidence boundaries, and explicit assumptions. The Evidence Ledger operationalizes those requirements by turning evidence management into a governed system rather than an informal research habit.

It serves five strategic roles:

1. **Traceability** — every meaningful claim should be traceable to an identified evidence source or explicitly marked as inferential.
2. **Auditability** — reviewers must be able to verify what evidence was used, when it was gathered, and how strong it is.
3. **Freshness control** — the system must know which conclusions are vulnerable to staleness.
4. **Contradiction handling** — conflicting evidence must be surfaced and governed, not silently collapsed.
5. **Cross-document continuity** — evidence used in EA, T1–T10, and later companion documents must be linkable across the full lifecycle.

This document is therefore a **governance backbone** rather than a narrative analysis template.

---

## 3. What This Document Is

This document is:

- a structured ledger for research evidence
- a control mechanism for source quality and claim support
- a freshness and contradiction registry
- a cross-reference layer between sources and analytical outputs
- a reusable artifact that persists beyond any single report

---

## 4. What This Document Is Not

The Evidence Ledger is **not**:

- an ecosystem analysis
- a market summary
- a bibliography without structure
- a notes dump
- a quote repository without claim linkage
- a substitute for judgment
- a place to hide unsupported assertions

It does not perform the analysis itself. It governs the evidence used to produce analysis.

---

## 5. When to Commission or Use It

The Evidence Ledger should be created at the start of any formal ecosystem research effort and maintained continuously throughout the lifecycle of that effort.

It should be mandatory whenever any of the following are true:

- a formal Ecosystem Analysis is being produced
- one or more Intelligence or Strategy templates are being commissioned
- multiple analysts or agents are contributing to the same body of work
- the work will inform strategic, capital, platform, or product decisions
- conclusions may need to be refreshed later
- the analysis may be audited or red-teamed

It should not be deferred until the end.

The ledger must be built alongside the work, not reconstructed after the fact.

---

## 6. Mandatory vs Conditional Use

**Mandatory** for:

- Ecosystem Analysis Standard work
- all T1–T10 template work
- T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register
- T13 Executive Decision Memo
- T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief
- T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard
- T16 Refresh & Monitoring Protocol
- T17 Platform Access & Constraint Audit
- T18 Cross-Ecosystem Portfolio Scorecard
- T19 Learning Capture Memo

**Conditional** for:

- low-stakes exploratory scans
- internal brainstorming that is explicitly not decision-bearing
- quick directional research where no strategic commitment is being made

Even in conditional cases, the ledger is recommended where practical.

---

## 7. Inputs Required

The Evidence Ledger requires the following inputs:

### 7.1 Source Inputs
- primary documentation
- official policy materials
- regulatory documents
- first-party company materials
- market data providers
- technical documentation
- earnings materials and filings where relevant
- credible secondary analysis where primary evidence is insufficient
- direct observations or field notes when explicitly captured

### 7.2 Analytical Inputs
- claim statements from EA and T1–T19
- key judgments or rankings
- inferred conclusions
- assumptions requiring support or challenge
- contradictions discovered during research

### 7.3 Administrative Inputs
- research date
- analyst or agent identifier
- collection method
- relevance classification
- freshness window or expected decay rate

---

## 8. Outputs Produced

The Evidence Ledger produces the following outputs:

- a governed inventory of sources
- explicit claim-to-source linkage
- source quality classifications
- contradiction records
- freshness and staleness signals
- evidence coverage diagnostics
- unresolved evidence gaps
- reusable audit trail for later review or refresh

These outputs should support every later document in the system.

---

## 9. Position in Sequencing Logic

T11 should be generated **before** or **at the same time as** formal analysis begins.

It sits in the sequence as follows:

1. opportunity or scope defined
2. evidence collection begins
3. **T11 Evidence Ledger established**
4. EA and selective T1–T10 work proceeds
5. T12 assumptions and unknowns formalized
6. T13 decision compression created
7. post-T10 conversion and validation work proceeds
8. refresh and learning workflows update the ledger continuously

The ledger is therefore both an early-stage and persistent artifact.

---

## 10. Relationship to Other Documents

### Upstream Relationships
The ledger may receive scoping context from intake or commissioning materials, but it does not depend on a completed analytical document to begin.

### Downstream Relationships
The ledger directly supports:

- **Ecosystem Analysis Standard** by providing traceable evidence support
- **T1–T10** by mapping claims, rankings, and conclusions to evidence
- **T12** by clarifying which assumptions exist because evidence is incomplete
- **T13** by enabling decision memos to cite evidence strength rather than rhetoric
- **T14** by preserving vector-to-concept lineage
- **T15** by clarifying what remains unvalidated
- **T16** by signaling which evidence is stale or at risk of staleness
- **T17** by capturing platform rules, constraints, and policy volatility evidence
- **T18** by enabling cross-ecosystem comparison on comparable evidence footing
- **T19** by recording where the original evidence base proved correct or insufficient

---

## 11. Core Analytical Questions

The Evidence Ledger should be designed so that a reviewer can answer the following questions quickly:

1. What evidence supports this claim?
2. Is the evidence primary, secondary, observational, inferential, or speculative?
3. How current is the evidence?
4. How credible is the source in this context?
5. Are there contradictory sources?
6. Has the contradiction been resolved, deferred, or left open?
7. Which sections of the operating system depend on this evidence?
8. Which conclusions are highly evidence-backed, and which are more interpretive?
9. What information is missing?
10. What would need to change for this conclusion to be revisited?

---

## 12. Required Structure of the Ledger

The Evidence Ledger should contain the following core sections.

### 12.1 Header
- ecosystem name
- scope name or project name
- version number
- research window
- last updated date
- owner / maintainer
- status

### 12.2 Source Registry
A structured list of all sources used or considered.

### 12.3 Claim Linkage Table
A table that maps claims to supporting evidence.

### 12.4 Contradiction Register
A table for evidence conflicts, inconsistencies, or disputes.

### 12.5 Freshness Monitor
A section that flags time-sensitive evidence and expected review thresholds.

### 12.6 Coverage Diagnostics
A summary of what is well-supported, weakly supported, missing, or over-dependent on thin evidence.

### 12.7 Evidence Gap Log
A registry of unanswered questions or claims that remain under-supported.

### 12.8 Change Log
A record of ledger updates over time.

---

## 13. Required Data Fields

At minimum, every ledger entry should contain the following fields.

### 13.1 Source Registry Fields
- **Source ID**
- **Source title**
- **Source type**
- **Publisher / origin**
- **Author or issuing body**
- **Publication date**
- **Access date**
- **Jurisdiction / market relevance**
- **URL or retrieval location**
- **Primary / secondary / tertiary classification**
- **Evidence modality** (policy, data, interview, documentation, observation, filing, etc.)
- **Authority rating**
- **Freshness rating**
- **Reliability notes**
- **Scope relevance**
- **Usage status** (used / considered / rejected / superseded)

### 13.2 Claim Linkage Fields
- **Claim ID**
- **Claim statement**
- **Document / section where claim appears**
- **Supporting Source IDs**
- **Contradicting Source IDs**
- **Support strength**
- **Inference level**
- **Confidence level**
- **Analyst note**
- **Refresh sensitivity**

### 13.3 Contradiction Register Fields
- **Contradiction ID**
- **Claim or question affected**
- **Source IDs in conflict**
- **Nature of conflict**
- **Severity**
- **Resolution status**
- **Resolution rationale**
- **Escalation required?**

### 13.4 Evidence Gap Fields
- **Gap ID**
- **Question unanswered**
- **Why gap exists**
- **Decision impact**
- **Severity**
- **Recommended next source or method**
- **Owner**
- **Status**

---

## 14. Source Classification Rules

All sources must be classified in a way that allows the system to distinguish strong evidence from weak evidence.

### 14.1 Primary Sources
Examples include:
- official platform documentation
- regulatory filings
- company earnings materials
- first-party policies
- technical specifications from the issuer
- official marketplace requirements

Primary sources should be preferred wherever available.

### 14.2 Secondary Sources
Examples include:
- reputable analyst commentary
- industry publications
- trusted market research summaries
- credible press reporting used to interpret a primary event

Secondary sources may support context, synthesis, and external interpretation, but should not quietly replace primary evidence when primary evidence exists.

### 14.3 Tertiary or Low-Control Sources
Examples include:
- uncontrolled commentary
- hearsay summaries
- reposted claims without traceable origin
- community statements without verification

These may occasionally surface leads, but they should not carry core analytical load unless explicitly marked and justified.

---

## 15. Authority Rating Framework

Each source must receive an authority rating appropriate to context.

Recommended scale:

- **A — Authoritative:** direct, official, highly relevant, and current
- **B — Strong:** credible and relevant, but not fully canonical
- **C — Useful but limited:** partially credible, contextual, or incomplete
- **D — Weak:** low-confidence, weakly attributable, or highly indirect
- **E — Unacceptable:** should not be used for support

Authority must be judged relative to the claim being supported.

A source can be A-level for one question and C-level for another.

---

## 16. Freshness Rating Framework

Because some evidence decays faster than others, each source should receive a freshness rating.

Recommended categories:

- **F1 — Highly time-sensitive**
- **F2 — Moderately time-sensitive**
- **F3 — Slowly changing**
- **F4 — Structurally stable**

Examples:
- policy updates, pricing, roadmap clues, and marketplace rules may be F1
- annual reports may be F2 or F3 depending on use
- foundational ecosystem structure may be F3 or F4

Freshness must be recorded independently from authority.

A source may be authoritative but stale.

---

## 17. Support Strength Rules

Claims should not all be treated equally. The ledger must distinguish support strength.

Recommended categories:

- **Directly supported** — clearly established by source evidence
- **Strongly supported** — not explicit in one source, but strongly substantiated by multiple sources
- **Conditionally supported** — plausible but dependent on assumptions or incomplete evidence
- **Weakly supported** — thin evidence; use caution
- **Unsupported** — no acceptable support found

Unsupported claims should not appear in strategic outputs unless explicitly framed as hypotheses.

---

## 18. Inference Level Rules

The ledger must mark whether a claim is evidence-derived or analyst-constructed.

Recommended categories:

- **I0 — Descriptive fact**
- **I1 — Low inference**
- **I2 — Moderate inference**
- **I3 — High inference / synthesis**
- **I4 — Strategic hypothesis**

This is necessary because many of the system’s most valuable outputs are not simple facts; they are judgments. The ledger should not suppress judgment. It should govern it.

---

## 19. Confidence Handling

Confidence should reflect the relationship between evidence strength, contradiction level, and inference load.

Recommended fields:
- high confidence
- moderate confidence
- provisional confidence
- low confidence

Confidence should not be assigned based on writing quality or analyst certainty. It must reflect evidentiary condition.

---

## 20. Contradiction Handling Standard

Contradictions must be recorded whenever:

- two sources disagree materially
- one source appears to supersede another
- evidence differs by geography, segment, or time frame
- the interpretation of a source is contested
- platform or policy language is ambiguous enough to support multiple readings

Contradictions should never be quietly ignored.

Each contradiction must be assigned one of the following statuses:

- resolved
- unresolved but low impact
- unresolved and decision-relevant
- pending additional evidence

Any unresolved contradiction that affects T10, T13, T14, T15, T17, or T18 should be escalated visibly.

---

## 21. Evidence Gap Standard

A formal gap should be logged whenever:

- an important question lacks acceptable evidence
- a key conclusion depends on a thin base of support
- evidence exists but is outdated relative to decision stakes
- access constraints prevented collection of needed evidence
- the ecosystem is shifting too quickly for older evidence to remain reliable

Gaps are not failures. Ungoverned gaps are failures.

---

## 22. Required Usage Rules

The following rules are mandatory.

### Rule 1 — No silent sourcing
No strategic claim should appear in formal outputs without either:
- linked evidence, or
- explicit labeling as inference, assumption, or hypothesis

### Rule 2 — No hidden contradictions
Contradictory evidence must be logged.

### Rule 3 — No stale evidence masquerading as current evidence
Time-sensitive evidence must be freshness-scored.

### Rule 4 — No single-source fragility for major conclusions
Major rankings, vectors, or platform judgments should not depend on one weak source where broader evidence is available.

### Rule 5 — No undifferentiated source lists
A simple bibliography is insufficient. Source function and support role must be explicit.

### Rule 6 — No evidence laundering through summary language
An unsupported inference cannot be made to look stronger by being stated elegantly.

---

## 23. Recommended Operating Procedure

### Step 1 — Register sources as they are encountered
Do not wait until the report is finished.

### Step 2 — Assign source classifications
Record authority, freshness, modality, and relevance.

### Step 3 — Link claims to sources continuously
As analytical writing develops, update the claim linkage table.

### Step 4 — Record contradictions and gaps immediately
Do not defer conflict logging.

### Step 5 — Review evidence coverage before major decisions
Prior to T10 or T13 release, examine weakly supported areas.

### Step 6 — Update ledger during refresh cycles
When the market changes, the ledger should be revised before or alongside narrative documents.

### Step 7 — Use the ledger in learning capture
When real-world outcomes diverge from prior conclusions, update the evidence trail.

---

## 24. Quality Standard / Acceptance Criteria

The Evidence Ledger should be considered acceptable only if all of the following are true:

1. All strategically meaningful claims in formal outputs can be traced to evidence or clearly marked inference.
2. Sources are classified by type, authority, and freshness.
3. Contradictions are visible and governed.
4. Evidence gaps are explicitly logged.
5. Major conclusions do not rely on unexamined source fragility.
6. The ledger is structured enough to support red-team review.
7. The ledger is reusable during refresh and post-launch learning.
8. A reviewer can determine which parts of the system are strongly grounded and which remain provisional.

---

## 25. Failure Modes and Misuse Warnings

Common failure modes include:

### 25.1 Bibliography masquerading as governance
A long source list without claim linkage is not a ledger.

### 25.2 Post hoc reconstruction
If the ledger is built after conclusions are finalized, evidence discipline will degrade.

### 25.3 Overweighting official sources without context
Official sources may be authoritative about policy, but not always about market experience, behavioral reality, or practical friction.

### 25.4 False precision
A detailed ledger does not guarantee correct conclusions.

### 25.5 Freshness blindness
Even excellent evidence decays.

### 25.6 Inference concealment
Analyst synthesis must be marked, not smuggled in as direct fact.

### 25.7 Non-maintenance
A ledger that is not updated becomes a stale compliance artifact rather than a live governance system.

---

## 26. Source and Evidence Expectations

The ledger should follow these evidence preferences:

1. use primary evidence first where available
2. use credible secondary evidence to contextualize, compare, or triangulate
3. mark tertiary or low-control evidence clearly
4. separate observation from interpretation
5. preserve retrieval dates for all volatile sources
6. record when a source has been superseded or invalidated

Where evidence is unavailable, this fact should be recorded explicitly rather than patched over with speculation.

---

## 27. Minimum Ledger Templates

The following template structures should be included in implementation.

## 27.1 Source Registry Template
| Source ID | Title | Type | Origin | Pub Date | Access Date | Authority | Freshness | Relevance | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 27.2 Claim Linkage Template
| Claim ID | Claim Statement | Appears In | Supporting Sources | Contradicting Sources | Support Strength | Inference Level | Confidence | Refresh Sensitivity | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 27.3 Contradiction Register Template
| Contradiction ID | Claim / Question | Sources in Conflict | Conflict Type | Severity | Status | Resolution | Escalation Required |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 27.4 Evidence Gap Template
| Gap ID | Unanswered Question | Why Missing | Decision Impact | Severity | Next Source / Method | Owner | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 27.5 Change Log Template
| Change ID | Date | Change Made | Reason | Sections Affected | Performed By |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

---

## 28. Relationship to Agentic Research Systems

The Evidence Ledger should be designed for both human and agentic operation.

This means:

- fields should be discrete and machine-legible where possible
- claim IDs and source IDs should be stable
- contradiction and gap states should be enumerable
- retrieval dates should be standardized
- evidence linkage should be updateable incrementally

An agent should be able to contribute to the ledger without eroding evidentiary discipline.

---

## 29. Versioning Notes

The Evidence Ledger Standard should evolve when any of the following occur:

- repeated red-team reviews expose a structural weakness in evidence governance
- new source types become strategically important
- the operating system expands into new ecosystem categories
- contradiction handling proves insufficient in practice
- refresh operations reveal missing freshness controls
- post-launch learning reveals that support-strength scoring was too crude

Version updates should record what governance weakness prompted the revision.

---

## 30. Final Standard Statement

The Market-Intelligence Operating System is only as strong as its evidence discipline.

The Evidence Ledger exists to ensure that the system’s outputs are not merely persuasive artifacts, but governed judgments with traceable foundations, visible uncertainty, and refreshable integrity.

Without T11, the operating system can still produce intelligence.
With T11, it can produce intelligence that survives scrutiny.

---

## Appendix A — Recommended Enumerations

### Source Type Enumeration
- official documentation
- policy / legal
- filing / earnings
- product / platform material
- analyst report
- press / journalism
- interview / conversation
- field observation
- dataset
- pricing / packaging page
- technical specification
- marketplace listing
- community discussion

### Usage Status Enumeration
- used
- considered
- rejected
- superseded
- archived

### Resolution Status Enumeration
- resolved
- unresolved low impact
- unresolved decision-relevant
- pending evidence

### Confidence Enumeration
- high
- moderate
- provisional
- low

### Refresh Sensitivity Enumeration
- immediate
- near-term
- periodic
- low

---

## Appendix B — Implementation Guidance

For practical use, the Evidence Ledger may be maintained in:

- spreadsheet form
- database form
- structured markdown with stable IDs
- research repository tables
- analyst workflow tools with export capability

The format may vary.
The governance requirements may not.

FILE 5/22: t_12_assumption_unknowns_register_standard.md
