# T12 — Assumption & Unknowns Register Standard

## Document Status
**System:** Market-Intelligence Operating System  
**Layer:** Companion Governance Layer  
**Designation:** T12  
**Document Type:** Standard  
**Status:** Canonical Draft  
**Purpose Class:** Uncertainty Governance / Assumption Control / Validation Readiness

---

## 1. Purpose

The **Assumption & Unknowns Register** is the authoritative uncertainty-governance artifact for the Market-Intelligence Operating System.

Its function is to identify, classify, govern, and track the assumptions, unresolved questions, missing knowledge, interpretive leaps, and confidence boundaries that remain after evidence collection and analysis.

The register exists to ensure that the system does not confuse:

- evidence with inference
- inference with conviction
- conviction with certainty
- missing knowledge with resolved knowledge

Its role is not to eliminate uncertainty. Its role is to make uncertainty visible, bounded, actionable, and governable.

---

## 2. Strategic Role in the Operating System

The Market-Intelligence Operating System is designed to produce disciplined judgments about ecosystems, participants, strategy, timing, risk, and entry vectors. Those judgments inevitably contain assumptions.

Some assumptions arise because:

- the market is partially opaque
- evidence is incomplete or contradictory
- future behavior cannot be directly observed yet
- strategic synthesis requires interpretation beyond descriptive fact
- platform or ecosystem conditions are changing faster than the evidence base can stabilize

The Assumption & Unknowns Register exists to prevent those realities from being buried inside elegant writing.

It serves six strategic roles:

1. **Boundary setting** — clarifies what the system knows versus what it believes.
2. **Risk exposure** — identifies which assumptions carry real downstream decision risk.
3. **Validation readiness** — creates a direct bridge into experiment design and concept testing.
4. **Decision hygiene** — prevents overconfident executive compression.
5. **Refresh discipline** — highlights which conclusions are most vulnerable to new information.
6. **Learning-loop integrity** — allows future outcomes to be compared against explicit prior assumptions.

This document is therefore a core governance instrument, not a narrative template.

---

## 3. What This Document Is

This document is:

- a structured register of assumptions embedded in analysis
- a governed inventory of unknowns and unresolved questions
- a severity map for uncertainty exposure
- a bridge between research and validation
- a mechanism for preventing hidden fragility in strategic outputs

---

## 4. What This Document Is Not

The Assumption & Unknowns Register is **not**:

- a place to excuse weak research
- a substitute for evidence collection
- a brainstorming dump of every possible question
- a narrative risk memo
- a prediction log without decision linkage
- a vague disclaimer layer

It does not justify avoidable ignorance. It governs unavoidable uncertainty.

---

## 5. When to Commission or Use It

The register should be created once a body of formal ecosystem research begins to mature and meaningful judgments are being formed.

It becomes mandatory whenever any of the following are true:

- Ecosystem Analysis conclusions are being drafted
- T1–T10 templates contain rankings, strategic judgments, or inferred dynamics
- T13 Executive Decision Memo is being prepared
- T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion is being initiated
- T15 Validation & Experiment Design work is about to begin
- the work will influence capital, product, platform, or market-entry decisions

It should not be postponed until after a decision is made.

The register must exist before strategic compression is finalized.

---

## 6. Mandatory vs Conditional Use

**Mandatory** for:

- formal Ecosystem Analysis work
- all T1–T10 work that includes judgment, synthesis, or prioritization
- T13 Executive Decision Memo
- T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief
- T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard
- T16 Refresh & Monitoring Protocol
- T18 Cross-Ecosystem Portfolio Scorecard
- T19 Learning Capture Memo

**Conditionally recommended** for:

- exploratory ecosystem scans
- early framing exercises
- low-stakes opportunity landscaping that is not yet decision-bearing

Where uncertainty may later influence a major decision, the register should be established early.

---

## 7. Inputs Required

The Assumption & Unknowns Register requires the following inputs:

### 7.1 Evidence Inputs
- T11 Evidence Ledger
- contradiction records
- evidence gaps
- freshness risks
- support-strength and confidence patterns

### 7.2 Analytical Inputs
- Ecosystem Analysis conclusions
- T1–T10 judgments, rankings, maps, and vectors
- strategic interpretations
- scoring systems or prioritization decisions
- decision memos and concept-conversion logic

### 7.3 Operational Inputs
- decision horizon
- risk tolerance
- validation budget constraints
- time sensitivity of the opportunity
- whether the assumption affects build, go-to-market, access, trust, or monetization

---

## 8. Outputs Produced

The register produces the following outputs:

- a governed inventory of assumptions
- explicit separation between knowns, beliefs, and unknowns
- severity-ranked uncertainty map
- decision-critical assumption set
- validation candidate queue
- unresolved-question registry
- refresh-sensitive conclusion flags
- historical record of what the system believed before outcomes arrived

These outputs support strategic honesty and downstream testing discipline.

---

## 9. Position in Sequencing Logic

T12 should be developed after evidence and analytical work begin to generate judgments, but before those judgments are compressed into final strategic recommendations.

Recommended sequence:

1. scope defined
2. T11 Evidence Ledger active
3. EA and selective T1–T10 work proceed
4. **T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register established and populated**
5. T13 Executive Decision Memo prepared
6. T10 vectors or strategic options reviewed against assumptions
7. T14 concept conversion initiated
8. T15 validation plan built from highest-risk assumptions
9. T16 and T19 update the register as the market evolves and outcomes arrive

T12 therefore sits between analysis and action, but also persists beyond both.

---

## 10. Relationship to Other Documents

### Upstream Relationships
T12 depends especially on:

- **T11 Evidence Ledger** for support strength, contradictions, evidence gaps, and freshness constraints
- **Ecosystem Analysis** for structural claims and system-level judgments
- **T1–T10** for participant, cultural, strategic, temporal, trust, risk, capital, and vector assumptions

### Downstream Relationships
T12 directly supports:

- **T13 Executive Decision Memo** by preventing false decisiveness
- **T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief** by exposing what the vector assumes about demand, fit, access, or behavior
- **T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard** by identifying what must be tested first
- **T16 Refresh & Monitoring Protocol** by highlighting which conclusions are most vulnerable to change
- **T18 Cross-Ecosystem Portfolio Scorecard** by adjusting apparent attractiveness for uncertainty burden
- **T19 Learning Capture Memo** by enabling forecast-vs-reality comparison at the assumption level

---

## 11. Core Analytical Questions

The register should allow a reviewer to answer the following questions quickly:

1. What assumptions does this body of work rely on?
2. Which assumptions are explicit and which were previously implicit?
3. Which assumptions are harmless and which are decision-critical?
4. Which assumptions exist because evidence is missing, contradictory, stale, or interpretive?
5. What is genuinely unknown rather than merely unverified?
6. Which assumptions can be tested, and how?
7. Which assumptions should block progress until resolved?
8. Which unknowns matter now versus later?
9. Which outputs are most exposed if an assumption fails?
10. What did the system believe at the time the decision was made?

---

## 12. Required Structure of the Register

The Assumption & Unknowns Register should contain the following core sections.

### 12.1 Header
- ecosystem or project name
- version number
- owner / maintainer
- date created
- last updated date
- decision horizon
- status

### 12.2 Assumption Registry
A structured list of all meaningful assumptions embedded in the analytical stack.

### 12.3 Unknowns Registry
A structured list of unresolved questions, blind spots, opaque areas, and unavailable knowledge.

### 12.4 Severity Map
A summary of which assumptions or unknowns carry the greatest downstream risk.

### 12.5 Validation Queue
A prioritized list of assumptions that should be tested through T15 or other evidence-gathering methods.

### 12.6 Blocking Conditions
A section for assumptions or unknowns severe enough to pause or constrain forward movement.

### 12.7 Change Log
A record of how assumptions, unknowns, and statuses evolve over time.

---

## 13. Required Data Fields

At minimum, every assumption or unknown entry should contain the following fields.

### 13.1 Assumption Registry Fields
- **Assumption ID**
- **Assumption statement**
- **Type of assumption**
- **Where it appears**
- **Why it exists**
- **Evidence condition**
- **Decision relevance**
- **Impact area**
- **Severity**
- **Confidence in assumption**
- **Testability**
- **Proposed validation path**
- **Failure consequence**
- **Owner**
- **Status**

### 13.2 Unknowns Registry Fields
- **Unknown ID**
- **Question or unresolved area**
- **Category of unknown**
- **Why unknown persists**
- **Decision impact**
- **Urgency**
- **Can it be resolved?**
- **Recommended next method**
- **Owner**
- **Status**

### 13.3 Severity Map Fields
- **Item ID**
- **Item type**
- **Severity score / class**
- **Blast radius**
- **Time sensitivity**
- **Blocking?**
- **Linked outputs affected**

---

## 14. Assumption Type Framework

Each assumption must be categorized so the system understands what kind of fragility it is dealing with.

Recommended categories:

- **Behavioral assumption** — assumes participant behavior, motivation, adoption, or response
- **Structural assumption** — assumes something about ecosystem shape or force persistence
- **Strategic assumption** — assumes an entry vector, wedge, or positioning logic will hold
- **Trust assumption** — assumes credibility, legitimacy, or adoption thresholds can be crossed
- **Timing assumption** — assumes market timing, readiness, or rhythm conditions
- **Access assumption** — assumes platform access, approval, distribution, or operational feasibility
- **Monetization assumption** — assumes pricing power, willingness to pay, margin logic, or revenue path
- **Execution assumption** — assumes the organization can actually deliver on the requirement
- **Comparative assumption** — assumes one ecosystem, segment, or vector is stronger than another
- **Validation assumption** — assumes a test method is fit to reveal the truth needed

A single assumption may touch multiple domains, but one primary type should be assigned.

---

## 15. Unknowns Framework

Unknowns are not identical to assumptions.

An **assumption** is a proposition the analysis is currently leaning on.
An **unknown** is a gap or unresolved domain where the system does not yet know enough to make a stable claim.

Recommended unknown categories:

- missing data
- inaccessible evidence
- unresolved contradiction
- future-state ambiguity
- segment opacity
- operational blind spot
- platform policy uncertainty
- pricing uncertainty
- trust or adoption opacity
- competitive response uncertainty

The register must keep these distinct.

Unknowns become dangerous when quietly converted into assumptions without governance.

---

## 16. Why Assumptions Exist

Every assumption should record why it exists. Recommended reasons include:

- evidence incomplete
- evidence contradictory
- evidence stale
- evidence too costly to gather now
- future behavior cannot be observed directly
- inference required for strategic synthesis
- access limitation prevented confirmation
- platform or regulatory ambiguity remains unresolved

This matters because not all assumptions are equally blameworthy.
Some are unavoidable. Some are signs of weak process.

---

## 17. Decision Relevance Framework

Each assumption or unknown should be ranked by how directly it affects decisions.

Recommended categories:

- **Critical** — could materially change go / no-go, vector ranking, concept selection, or ecosystem choice
- **High** — unlikely to reverse the whole decision alone, but could materially distort execution or prioritization
- **Moderate** — meaningful, but manageable within adaptive execution
- **Low** — useful context, limited consequence if wrong

No executive decision memo should treat all assumptions as equally important.

---

## 18. Impact Area Framework

Each item should record which part of the system it threatens.

Recommended impact areas:

- ecosystem selection
- segment selection
- interface selection
- vector ranking
- concept translation
- validation design
- pricing / monetization
- trust acquisition
- platform access
- operational feasibility
- timing / launch window
- portfolio prioritization

This helps reveal where uncertainty is clustered.

---

## 19. Severity Framework

Severity should reflect the combined effect of:

- decision relevance
- blast radius
- time sensitivity
- difficulty of recovery if wrong
- closeness to irreversible commitment

Recommended severity classes:

- **S1 — Critical / blocking**
- **S2 — High / decision-relevant**
- **S3 — Moderate / manageable**
- **S4 — Low / monitor**

Severity is not the same as confidence.
A low-confidence assumption may still be low severity if little depends on it.

---

## 20. Blast Radius Framework

The register should record how much damage occurs if the assumption fails.

Recommended categories:

- local
- multi-section
- system-wide
- decision-reversing

This prevents underestimating assumptions that sit beneath multiple outputs.

---

## 21. Confidence Handling

The register should capture the confidence level associated with the assumption itself.

Recommended categories:

- high confidence assumption
- moderate confidence assumption
- provisional assumption
- weak assumption

This does not mean the assumption is true.
It reflects how strong the current basis is for leaning on it.

---

## 22. Testability Framework

Not every assumption can be resolved in the same way. The register should record testability.

Recommended categories:

- directly testable now
- testable with moderate effort
- testable only after concept formation
- observable only over time
- currently not testable

This is essential for building a clean handoff into T15.

---

## 23. Status Framework

Each assumption and unknown must have an explicit status.

Recommended statuses:

- identified
- under review
- accepted provisionally
- validation required
- actively being tested
- resolved
- retired
- superseded
- blocked pending resolution

The register must show movement over time.
A static assumption list is not governance.

---

## 24. Blocking Conditions Standard

An assumption or unknown should be considered **blocking** when any of the following are true:

- its failure would reverse a go / no-go decision
- it materially undermines the selected ecosystem or platform
- it invalidates the current highest-ranked entry vector
- it directly threatens platform access or legality
- it makes monetization logic too speculative to proceed responsibly
- it creates a trust hurdle that is likely prohibitive
- the organization has no credible path to validate it before commitment

Blocking items should be surfaced prominently in T13 and T14.

---

## 25. Unknowns Triage Standard

Unknowns should be triaged according to actionability.

### 25.1 Resolve Now
Unknowns that materially affect imminent decisions and can be addressed through additional research or direct inquiry.

### 25.2 Test Later
Unknowns that matter, but are best resolved through structured validation rather than further desk research.

### 25.3 Monitor
Unknowns that are real but not yet decision-bearing.

### 25.4 Accept
Unknowns that cannot be resolved economically at this stage and should be accepted with explicit boundaries.

This prevents the system from becoming either reckless or paralyzed.

---

## 26. Required Usage Rules

The following rules are mandatory.

### Rule 1 — No hidden assumptions
If a strategic judgment depends on an assumption, that assumption must be registered.

### Rule 2 — No false certainty
Unknowns must not be collapsed into declarative confidence for rhetorical convenience.

### Rule 3 — No equal treatment of unequal uncertainty
Decision-critical assumptions must be distinguished from minor uncertainties.

### Rule 4 — No validation planning without assumption visibility
T15 should not be produced without drawing from T12.

### Rule 5 — No executive memo without uncertainty disclosure
T13 must cite major critical assumptions and blocking conditions.

### Rule 6 — No stale assumptions preserved by inertia
Assumptions must be revisited when evidence changes, markets shift, or experiments fail.

### Rule 7 — No assumption laundering through scoring systems
If a portfolio score, vector rank, or platform attractiveness rating depends on assumptions, the register must reveal that dependency.

---

## 27. Recommended Operating Procedure

### Step 1 — Extract assumptions from the analytical stack
Review EA and T1–T10 for hidden dependencies, strategic claims, and future-facing judgments.

### Step 2 — Separate assumptions from unknowns
Do not treat unresolved questions and active beliefs as the same thing.

### Step 3 — Classify and severity-rank each item
Assign type, relevance, impact area, severity, and blast radius.

### Step 4 — Identify blocking items
Flag assumptions or unknowns that should constrain forward movement.

### Step 5 — Build the validation queue
Move the highest-risk, most testable assumptions into a structured sequence for T15.

### Step 6 — Use the register in executive compression
Ensure T13 reflects critical assumptions honestly.

### Step 7 — Update after experiments or new evidence
As evidence improves, contradictions resolve, or validation occurs, revise the register.

### Step 8 — Feed outcomes into learning capture
When reality arrives, compare it against what the system previously assumed.

---

## 28. Quality Standard / Acceptance Criteria

The Assumption & Unknowns Register should be considered acceptable only if all of the following are true:

1. Major strategic judgments have their key assumptions surfaced explicitly.
2. Assumptions and unknowns are kept distinct.
3. Each item is classified by type, relevance, severity, and status.
4. Decision-critical and blocking items are visible.
5. The register can directly inform T13 and T15.
6. The system can identify which outputs are most exposed to assumption failure.
7. The register is updated when evidence or outcomes change.
8. A reviewer can see what the operating system knew, did not know, and was choosing to believe at the time of decision.

---

## 29. Failure Modes and Misuse Warnings

Common failure modes include:

### 29.1 Disclaimer theater
A vague note that “some assumptions exist” is not governance.

### 29.2 Overpopulation
If every minor interpretive nuance becomes an entry, the register loses signal.

### 29.3 Underpopulation
If only obvious assumptions are logged, hidden fragility remains embedded in the analysis.

### 29.4 Confusing uncertainty with weakness
A visible assumption register strengthens judgment. It does not weaken it.

### 29.5 Failing to distinguish testable from non-testable assumptions
Validation efforts become wasteful when this distinction is ignored.

### 29.6 Static treatment
An old assumption register becomes a historical artifact instead of a live control system.

### 29.7 Executive sanitization
If critical assumptions are stripped out when findings are summarized for decision-makers, the system fails at the point of highest consequence.

---

## 30. Source and Evidence Expectations

The register should draw from T11 rather than freehand opinion.

Each assumption should, where possible, reference:

- the evidence condition that gave rise to it
- contradictions or evidence gaps connected to it
- the outputs affected by it
- the best available path to strengthen, validate, or retire it

The register must not become a substitute for the Evidence Ledger.
It is a governance companion to the ledger, not a replacement.

---

## 31. Minimum Register Templates

The following template structures should be included in implementation.

## 31.1 Assumption Registry Template
| Assumption ID | Assumption Statement | Type | Appears In | Why It Exists | Evidence Condition | Decision Relevance | Impact Area | Severity | Blast Radius | Confidence | Testability | Proposed Validation Path | Failure Consequence | Owner | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 31.2 Unknowns Registry Template
| Unknown ID | Question / Unresolved Area | Category | Why Unknown Persists | Decision Impact | Urgency | Can It Be Resolved? | Recommended Next Method | Owner | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 31.3 Severity Map Template
| Item ID | Item Type | Severity | Blast Radius | Time Sensitivity | Blocking? | Outputs Affected | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 31.4 Validation Queue Template
| Priority | Item ID | Item Statement | Why Test Matters | Testability | Suggested Method | Decision Dependent | Owner | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

## 31.5 Change Log Template
| Change ID | Date | Change Made | Reason | Items Affected | Performed By |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

---

## 32. Relationship to Agentic Research Systems

The Assumption & Unknowns Register should be designed for both human and agentic use.

This means:

- stable IDs for assumptions and unknowns
- discrete enum-like fields where practical
- explicit linkage to T11 source and contradiction records
- clear status transitions
- direct machine-legible handoff into T15 and T19

An agent should be able to extract candidate assumptions from analytical text, but a reviewer must still govern severity, relevance, and blocking status.

The register should support semi-automated detection without surrendering judgment.

---

## 33. Versioning Notes

The Assumption & Unknowns Register Standard should evolve when any of the following occur:

- repeated work reveals recurring hidden assumptions that the framework does not capture well
- validation programs show that testability categories are too crude
- refresh cycles reveal that time sensitivity needs stronger handling
- portfolio comparison repeatedly fails to account for uncertainty burden
- post-launch learning shows that failure consequences were poorly modeled
- platform ecosystem work introduces new forms of access or policy uncertainty that deserve explicit treatment

Version updates should record which governance weakness or pattern prompted revision.

---

## 34. Final Standard Statement

A strong market-intelligence system does not pretend to know more than it knows.

The Assumption & Unknowns Register exists to make the system’s uncertainty legible, ranked, testable, and governable.

Without T12, the operating system can still sound confident.
With T12, it can become trustworthy under uncertainty.

---

## Appendix A — Recommended Enumerations

### Assumption Type Enumeration
- behavioral
- structural
- strategic
- trust
- timing
- access
- monetization
- execution
- comparative
- validation

### Unknown Category Enumeration
- missing data
- inaccessible evidence
- unresolved contradiction
- future-state ambiguity
- segment opacity
- operational blind spot
- platform policy uncertainty
- pricing uncertainty
- trust / adoption opacity
- competitive response uncertainty

### Decision Relevance Enumeration
- critical
- high
- moderate
- low

### Severity Enumeration
- S1 critical / blocking
- S2 high / decision-relevant
- S3 moderate / manageable
- S4 low / monitor

### Status Enumeration
- identified
- under review
- accepted provisionally
- validation required
- actively being tested
- resolved
- retired
- superseded
- blocked pending resolution

### Testability Enumeration
- directly testable now
- testable with moderate effort
- testable only after concept formation
- observable only over time
- currently not testable

---

## Appendix B — Implementation Guidance

For practical use, the Assumption & Unknowns Register may be maintained in:

- spreadsheet form
- database form
- structured markdown with stable IDs
- research repository tables
- linked records associated with T11 and T15 artifacts

The format may vary.
The governance requirements may not.

# T13 — Executive Decision Memo Standard

## Document Status
**System:** Market-Intelligence Operating System  
**Layer:** Companion Decision Layer  
**Designation:** T13  
**Document Type:** Standard  
**Status:** Canonical Draft  
**Purpose Class:** Decision Compression / Executive Briefing / Strategic Gating

---

## 1. Purpose

The **Executive Decision Memo** is the authoritative decision-compression artifact for the Market-Intelligence Operating System.

Its function is to translate the full analytical stack into a concise, decision-grade briefing that enables a founder, operator, investor, strategist, or leadership group to make a clear next decision without rereading the entire research corpus.

The memo exists to answer a practical problem: rigorous analysis often becomes too large, too distributed, or too conceptually dense to drive timely action. The Executive Decision Memo preserves rigor while compressing complexity.

Its purpose is not to simplify the market into slogans. Its purpose is to make the consequences of the analysis legible at the point of decision.

---

## 2. Strategic Role in the Operating System

The Market-Intelligence Operating System is designed to move from terrain understanding to deeper intelligence to strategic entry logic. That produces substantial analytical depth, but depth alone does not create an actionable decision.

The Executive Decision Memo serves seven strategic roles:

1. **Compression** — reduces the full research stack into the smallest form that still preserves decision integrity.
2. **Decision clarity** — defines the actual decision being asked for.
3. **Strategic gating** — determines whether the system is recommending advance, defer, redirect, or reject.
4. **Uncertainty preservation** — carries forward critical assumptions, contradictions, and no-go conditions rather than stripping them away.
5. **Prioritization** — makes the most important findings and vectors visible in ranked form.
6. **Alignment** — ensures different readers are reacting to the same distilled judgment.
7. **Handoff** — provides the clean bridge from analysis into concept conversion, validation, or portfolio allocation.

This document is therefore a strategic decision instrument, not a substitute for the full analysis.

---

## 3. What This Document Is

This document is:

- a decision-grade summary of the analytical stack
- a structured recommendation memo
- a gating mechanism between analysis and next action
- a compression artifact that preserves uncertainty and evidence quality
- a boardroom-usable strategic brief

---

## 4. What This Document Is Not

The Executive Decision Memo is **not**:

- a generic summary
- a pitch deck in prose form
- a motivational narrative
- a replacement for EA or T1–T10
- a place to introduce brand-new analysis
- a rhetorical sales document designed to force consensus
- a product brief

It should not create false certainty by omitting constraints, caveats, or evidence quality issues.

---

## 5. When to Commission or Use It

The memo should be created when the analytical work has matured enough to support a real decision, and before the organization commits to concept generation, validation investment, platform pursuit, or broader strategic allocation.

It becomes mandatory whenever any of the following are true:

- a go / no-go decision is imminent
- an ecosystem or platform must be prioritized against alternatives
- T10 has produced ranked entry vectors
- a concept-conversion effort is being considered
- leadership needs a decision artifact rather than a research archive
- the analysis will influence capital, product, partnership, or market-entry commitments

The memo should not be drafted too early. Compression before the analysis is mature will degrade judgment.

---

## 6. Mandatory vs Conditional Use

**Mandatory** for:

- ecosystem decisions that influence product or capital allocation
- post-T10 strategic review
- selection among multiple vectors, platforms, or ecosystems
- handoff into T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion
- portfolio prioritization using T18

**Conditionally recommended** for:

- smaller internal reviews where the full analytical stack is already shared and decision-makers are close to the work
- exploratory work that is still too immature for recommendation

Where stakes are meaningful, T13 should be treated as required.

---

## 7. Inputs Required

The Executive Decision Memo requires the following inputs:

### 7.1 Analytical Inputs
- Ecosystem Analysis conclusions
- relevant T1–T10 outputs
- ranked vectors, if produced
- key maps, tensions, risks, and leverage points
- strategic comparisons between options

### 7.2 Governance Inputs
- T11 Evidence Ledger
- T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register
- contradiction records
- evidence coverage and freshness conditions

### 7.3 Decision Inputs
- decision horizon
- strategic objective
- available resource context
- appetite for risk
- whether the memo is asking for selection, deferral, further study, or rejection

---

## 8. Outputs Produced

The memo produces the following outputs:

- a clearly defined decision statement
- a bounded recommendation
- ranked strategic options or vectors
- the decisive reasons supporting the recommendation
- critical assumptions and blocking conditions
- no-go criteria
- next action pathway
- an executive-level record of what the system was recommending at that time

These outputs should enable movement without severing the link to the deeper research base.

---

## 9. Position in Sequencing Logic

T13 should be produced after evidence and analysis are mature, after assumptions have been surfaced in T12, and before concept conversion or validation planning proceeds.

Recommended sequence:

1. scope defined
2. T11 Evidence Ledger active
3. EA and selective T1–T10 completed to decision-ready level
4. T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register populated
5. **T13 Executive Decision Memo prepared**
6. decision gate reached
7. if advancing, T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion begins
8. if validation needed, T15 is commissioned
9. if not advancing, the memo records defer / redirect / reject logic for future reference

T13 is the operating system’s primary decision gate artifact.

---

## 10. Relationship to Other Documents

### Upstream Relationships
T13 depends primarily on:

- **Ecosystem Analysis** for system-level structure and force logic
- **T1–T10** for deeper intelligence and strategic option formation
- **T11 Evidence Ledger** for evidentiary grounding
- **T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register** for uncertainty exposure and blocking conditions

### Downstream Relationships
T13 directly supports:

- **T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief** by stating which vector or option is being advanced
- **T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard** by clarifying which assumptions require testing before commitment
- **T16 Refresh & Monitoring Protocol** by identifying time-sensitive conclusions
- **T18 Cross-Ecosystem Portfolio Scorecard** by providing comparable decision outputs across ecosystems
- **T19 Learning Capture Memo** by serving as the record of what was recommended and why

---

## 11. Core Analytical Questions

The memo should allow an executive reader to answer the following questions quickly:

1. What decision is being asked for?
2. What is the recommendation?
3. Why is that recommendation justified?
4. What alternatives were considered and why were they not selected?
5. What assumptions or unknowns could overturn the recommendation?
6. What no-go conditions would force a pause or rejection?
7. How time-sensitive is this decision?
8. What should happen next if the recommendation is accepted?
9. What should happen next if the recommendation is not accepted?
10. How confident should the decision-maker be in this recommendation?

---

## 12. Required Structure of the Memo

The Executive Decision Memo should contain the following core sections.

### 12.1 Header
- ecosystem / project name
- memo version
- date
- owner / author
- decision horizon
- status

### 12.2 Decision Statement
A precise statement of the decision being requested.

### 12.3 Recommendation
A concise statement of the recommended path.

### 12.4 Why This Recommendation
A compressed explanation of the decisive findings and strategic logic.

### 12.5 Options Considered
A ranked set of alternatives, including why the selected option outranks them.

### 12.6 Critical Assumptions and Unknowns
A focused carry-forward of the most important T12 items.

### 12.7 Risks, Constraints, and No-Go Conditions
The conditions under which the recommendation should not proceed.

### 12.8 Timing Considerations
A statement of urgency, sequencing, windows, or reasons to defer.

### 12.9 Recommended Next Step
The immediate next action if the decision is accepted.

### 12.10 Evidence and Confidence Note
A concise statement of evidence quality, freshness, and confidence boundary.

### 12.11 Appendices or References
Pointers back to the deeper documents for audit or deeper review.

---

## 13. Required Data Fields

At minimum, every memo should include the following fields.

### 13.1 Header Fields
- **Memo ID**
- **Ecosystem / project name**
- **Version**
- **Date**
- **Prepared by**
- **Decision owner**
- **Decision horizon**
- **Status**

### 13.2 Decision Fields
- **Decision requested**
- **Recommendation category**
- **Strategic objective supported**
- **Decision deadline or timing pressure**

### 13.3 Recommendation Fields
- **Selected option / vector / ecosystem**
- **Rank**
- **Rationale summary**
- **Expected upside**
- **Primary constraints**

### 13.4 Uncertainty Fields
- **Critical assumption IDs**
- **Blocking condition IDs**
- **Major contradictions affecting recommendation**
- **Confidence level**
- **Freshness sensitivity**

### 13.5 Next-Step Fields
- **Immediate next action**
- **Required downstream document**
- **Owner**
- **Timing**

---

## 14. Decision Category Framework

Each memo must state what kind of decision it is asking for.

Recommended categories:

- **Advance** — proceed into the next structured step
- **Defer** — hold due to timing, evidence, or constraint conditions
- **Redirect** — change ecosystem, vector, segment, or interface focus
- **Reject** — do not proceed
- **Compare further** — additional targeted analysis is needed before selection

The category should be explicit.

---

## 15. Recommendation Logic Standard

A strong recommendation must state not only what to do, but why the selected path outranks alternatives.

This requires the memo to distinguish between:

- decisive reasons
- supporting reasons
- contextual reasons
- unresolved reasons that remain under uncertainty

The recommendation should be based on the strongest strategic logic revealed by the full stack, not on what sounds simplest or most emotionally appealing.

---

## 16. Options Considered Standard

The memo must show that alternatives were considered in a disciplined way.

Recommended fields for each option:

- option name
- rank
- strategic attractiveness
- access feasibility
- trust difficulty
- timing fit
- capital capture logic
- key reason not selected

The memo should not pretend the chosen recommendation was the only conceivable path.

---

## 17. Critical Assumptions and Unknowns Standard

The memo must include only the most decision-relevant assumptions and unknowns from T12.

These should be selected based on:

- ability to overturn the recommendation
- relevance to next-step execution
- severity or blocking status
- closeness to irreversible commitment

The memo should not reproduce the entire T12 register.
It should carry forward only the assumptions that matter most at decision time.

---

## 18. No-Go Conditions Standard

The memo must explicitly state the conditions under which the recommendation should not proceed.

Recommended no-go condition categories:

- platform access failure
- evidence deterioration or contradictory update
- monetization logic too speculative
- trust barrier too severe
- timing window no longer favorable
- validation threshold not met
- key assumption fails or remains unresolvable
- execution burden exceeds viable capacity

This prevents the memo from functioning as a one-way advocacy device.

---

## 19. Timing Considerations Standard

The memo must address timing directly.

Recommended timing questions:

- Is this a now decision, a later decision, or a monitor-only situation?
- What creates urgency?
- What creates reason to wait?
- What decays if the decision is delayed?
- What may improve if the decision is delayed?

Timing should reflect T7 and T16 where relevant, but in compressed form.

---

## 20. Confidence Handling

The memo must not collapse evidence quality, freshness, and assumption burden into vague confidence language.

Recommended confidence framing:

- **High confidence recommendation** — strong evidence, manageable uncertainty, low contradiction burden
- **Moderate confidence recommendation** — good directional basis, but important uncertainties remain
- **Provisional recommendation** — a path is favored, but major assumptions or time-sensitive evidence require caution
- **Low confidence recommendation** — not ready for commitment; likely defer, compare further, or reject

Confidence should reflect evidentiary condition, not executive appetite.

---

## 21. Evidence Note Standard

The memo must include a short evidence note covering:

- overall evidence strength
- notable freshness risks
- presence of unresolved contradictions
- whether critical conclusions are heavily inferential

This ensures that the memo remains connected to T11 rather than operating as pure narrative.

---

## 22. Recommended Next-Step Standard

The memo must end with a clear immediate next step.

Recommended next-step pathways:

- commission T14 for a selected vector
- commission T15 for validation on a constrained concept or assumption set
- perform targeted additional research on one blocking issue
- move into portfolio comparison via T18
- defer and monitor under T16
- close the opportunity and archive under reject logic

The memo should not end in analytical ambiguity.
It must specify what operational move follows from the recommendation.

---

## 23. Required Usage Rules

The following rules are mandatory.

### Rule 1 — One memo, one real decision
The memo must state the exact decision being requested.

### Rule 2 — No false compression
Do not omit critical assumptions, contradictions, or no-go conditions in the name of brevity.

### Rule 3 — No new analysis smuggled into the memo
The memo compresses existing analysis. It does not invent conclusions on the fly.

### Rule 4 — No advocacy masquerading as judgment
The memo should not be written to force a predetermined answer.

### Rule 5 — No unsupported ranking language
If an option is ranked first, the strategic basis for that ranking must be visible.

### Rule 6 — No next-step ambiguity
The memo must indicate what should happen immediately if the decision is accepted.

### Rule 7 — No uncertainty stripping
T12 must be reflected honestly.

---

## 24. Recommended Operating Procedure

### Step 1 — Define the exact decision
Clarify whether the memo is about ecosystem selection, vector selection, platform access, timing, concept advance, or rejection.

### Step 2 — Extract the decisive findings
Identify the smallest set of analytical conclusions that materially determine the recommendation.

### Step 3 — Rank the options
Show what alternatives were considered and how they compare.

### Step 4 — Pull critical assumptions from T12
Carry forward only the items that matter at this decision gate.

### Step 5 — Define no-go conditions
State what would make the recommendation invalid or unsafe to pursue.

### Step 6 — Write the recommendation and next step
Make the decision and the immediate operational implication explicit.

### Step 7 — Attach evidence and confidence note
Ensure the memo remains grounded in T11 and bounded by T12.

### Step 8 — Use the memo as the decision record
Archive it as the formal statement of what was recommended and why.

---

## 25. Quality Standard / Acceptance Criteria

The Executive Decision Memo should be considered acceptable only if all of the following are true:

1. The decision being requested is explicit.
2. The recommendation is clear and bounded.
3. The decisive reasons are visible and traceable to the broader analytical stack.
4. Relevant alternatives were considered and ranked.
5. Critical assumptions and blocking conditions are visible.
6. Timing and urgency are addressed directly.
7. The next action is operationally clear.
8. The memo preserves evidence quality and confidence boundaries.
9. A decision-maker can act from the memo without being misled about uncertainty.

---

## 26. Failure Modes and Misuse Warnings

Common failure modes include:

### 26.1 Summary without decision
A compact recap of analysis is not a decision memo if it never states what must be decided.

### 26.2 Advocacy drift
If the memo is written to “sell” one option rather than judge it, strategic discipline degrades.

### 26.3 Uncertainty laundering
Stripping out assumptions and contradictions to make the memo sound cleaner makes the system less trustworthy.

### 26.4 Overcompression
If important distinctions between options are lost, the memo may create a false impression of clarity.

### 26.5 No-go omission
A recommendation without stop conditions is incomplete.

### 26.6 Next-step blur
If the memo ends with vague language rather than a clear downstream action, it fails as a gating artifact.

### 26.7 Executive sanitization
If the memo becomes polished beyond usefulness and ceases to reflect actual evidence quality, it has become theater.

---

## 27. Source and Evidence Expectations

The memo should not cite every underlying source directly, but it must be tethered to T11 and T12.

At minimum it should reference:

- the analytical documents synthesized
- the evidence quality condition
- the critical assumption set
- any unresolved contradiction that could materially affect the recommendation

The memo is not a substitute for evidence traceability.
It is a compression layer built on top of evidence governance.

---

## 28. Minimum Memo Template

The following structure should be included in implementation.

## 28.1 Executive Decision Memo Template

### Header
- Memo ID
- Ecosystem / Project
- Version
- Date
- Prepared By
- Decision Owner
- Decision Horizon
- Status

### 1. Decision Requested
[State the exact decision]

### 2. Recommendation
[Advance / Defer / Redirect / Reject / Compare Further]

### 3. Why This Recommendation
- Decisive reason 1
- Decisive reason 2
- Decisive reason 3

### 4. Options Considered
| Option | Rank | Why It Was Considered | Why It Was Not Selected / Why It Ranked Lower |
|---|---|---|---|

### 5. Critical Assumptions and Unknowns
| Item ID | Statement | Severity | Why It Matters | Blocking? |
|---|---|---|---|---|

### 6. Risks, Constraints, and No-Go Conditions
| Condition | Type | Severity | Action if Triggered |
|---|---|---|---|

### 7. Timing Considerations
[Urgency, sequencing, windows, or reasons to wait]

### 8. Recommended Next Step
[Specific downstream action]

### 9. Evidence and Confidence Note
[Summary of evidence quality, freshness, contradictions, and confidence]

### 10. Supporting References
- Ecosystem Analysis
- relevant T-documents
- T11
- T12

---

## 29. Relationship to Agentic Research Systems

The Executive Decision Memo should be designed so that agents can draft it, but not so that judgment is surrendered to automation.

This means:

- decision categories should be standardized
- options and ranks should be discrete and comparable
- assumption IDs and no-go conditions should be stable references
- evidence and confidence notes should be drawn from governed upstream artifacts
- the final recommendation should remain reviewable by a human decision-maker

An agent may compress the stack.
The operating system must still govern whether the compression is faithful.

---

## 30. Versioning Notes

The Executive Decision Memo Standard should evolve when any of the following occur:

- decision-makers repeatedly misread the memo’s level of confidence
- important no-go conditions are routinely omitted
- memo structure proves too long or too thin for actual strategic use
- portfolio comparison requires tighter normalization across memos
- learning capture shows that decisive reasons were poorly chosen or misleadingly ranked
- post-T10 workflows require a more explicit bridge into T14 and T15

Version updates should record what decision-quality weakness prompted the change.

---

## 31. Final Standard Statement

A rigorous market-intelligence system needs more than analysis. It needs a disciplined way to decide.

The Executive Decision Memo exists to compress a deep research stack into a form that supports action without amputating uncertainty, evidence quality, or strategic nuance.

Without T13, the operating system can produce insight.
With T13, it can produce decision-ready judgment.

---

## Appendix B — Implementation Guidance

For practical use, the Executive Decision Memo may be maintained in:

- structured markdown
- decision memo repository format
- linked database records connected to T11 and T12
- presentation-adjacent narrative documents for executive review

The format may vary.
The decision discipline may not.

# T14 — Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief Standard

## Document Status
**System:** Market-Intelligence Operating System  
**Layer:** Companion Conversion Layer  
**Designation:** T14  
**Document Type:** Standard  
**Status:** Canonical Draft  
**Purpose Class:** Strategy-to-Concept Translation / Opportunity Structuring / Post-T10 Conversion Control

---

## 1. Purpose

The **Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief** is the authoritative translation artifact for converting a selected strategic entry vector into one or more bounded concept candidates.

Its function is to ensure that the operating system does not jump directly from market strategy into loose ideation, feature lists, or product enthusiasm. Instead, it creates a disciplined bridge from strategic logic to concept formation.

The brief exists to answer a recurring problem: a strong strategic vector often degrades once teams begin “brainstorming the product.” The original market logic becomes diluted, overwritten by preference, or replaced by generic solutioning. T14 prevents that drift.

Its purpose is to preserve fidelity between:

- the market forces identified upstream
- the entry vector selected in T10 / T13
- the concept candidates explored downstream

---

## 2. Strategic Role in the Operating System

The Market-Intelligence Operating System is designed to stop at ranked strategic entry vectors before build-stage product thinking begins. That discipline is necessary, but it creates a handoff challenge: once the system has identified where to enter, someone still has to define what to build or offer.

T14 serves eight strategic roles:

1. **Translation** — converts strategic vectors into concept-ready form.
2. **Lineage preservation** — ensures concepts can be traced back to strategic rationale.
3. **Boundary setting** — prevents concept sprawl and premature feature inflation.
4. **Constraint carrying** — preserves trust, timing, platform, monetization, and access realities identified upstream.
5. **Variant generation** — allows multiple concept pathways to emerge from a single vector without losing discipline.
6. **Validation readiness** — structures concepts so they can flow into T15.
7. **Strategic coherence** — keeps concept logic aligned with the ecosystem rather than internal preference.
8. **Decision accountability** — creates a record of how a strategic judgment became an actionable concept candidate.

T14 is therefore the operating system’s controlled translation layer between strategy and validation.

---

## 3. What This Document Is

This document is:

- a conversion brief from vector to concept
- a strategic translation artifact
- a constraint-preserving handoff document
- a bounded concept-formation standard
- a precursor to structured validation

---

## 4. What This Document Is Not

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief is **not**:

- a freeform product brainstorm
- a feature backlog
- a PRD
- a design brief for full implementation
- a founder vision note detached from market logic
- a marketing narrative written before the concept is validated
- a replacement for T10 or T13

It should not be used to smuggle ad hoc ideas into the pipeline without strategic lineage.

---

## 5. When to Commission or Use It

T14 should be commissioned after a strategic vector, ecosystem pathway, or ranked option has been selected for advancement and before full validation planning or product specification begins.

It becomes mandatory whenever any of the following are true:

- T10 has produced a selected vector worth exploring further
- T13 has recommended advance on a strategic path
- one or more concepts must be derived from a market opportunity rather than invented from scratch
- the organization wants concept candidates that remain faithful to upstream analysis
- T15 validation planning is about to begin

T14 should not be generated before strategic selection is mature.

Premature conversion invites incoherent concept formation.

---

## 6. Mandatory vs Conditional Use

**Mandatory** for:

- any effort moving from T10 / T13 into concept exploration
- any concept path intended to feed T15 validation
- any ecosystem opportunity where platform access, trust, monetization, or timing constraints materially shape concept design
- any multi-concept comparison effort derived from a single vector

**Conditionally recommended** for:

- very early idea generation where no strategic vector has yet been selected
- low-stakes creative exploration not yet tied to the operating system’s formal decision path

Where concept work is meant to remain disciplined, T14 should be treated as required.

---

## 7. Inputs Required

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief requires the following inputs:

### 7.1 Strategic Inputs
- T10 ranked strategic entry vectors
- T13 Executive Decision Memo
- selected ecosystem, platform, interface, or segment pathway
- core leverage logic from upstream analysis

### 7.2 Analytical Inputs
- relevant EA conclusions
- relevant T1–T9 findings, especially trust, timing, risk, capital flow, participant decision structure, and competitive topology
- force dynamics and friction points being targeted

### 7.3 Governance Inputs
- T11 Evidence Ledger
- T12 Assumption & Unknowns Register
- decision-critical assumptions and blocking conditions
- unresolved contradictions or platform constraints

### 7.4 Operating Inputs
- resource context
- intended validation scope
- acceptable concept complexity at this stage
- whether the path is commercial software, service layer, workflow tool, ecosystem extension, or other form

---

## 8. Outputs Produced

T14 produces the following outputs:

- a clearly stated source vector and its market rationale
- one or more bounded concept candidates derived from that vector
- concept logic tied to ecosystem forces and participant needs
- constraints that must govern concept shape
- explicit value hypotheses
- trust and access requirements carried into concept design
- initial monetization logic
- a structured bridge into T15 validation planning

These outputs should preserve strategic clarity while making controlled concept generation possible.

---

## 9. Position in Sequencing Logic

T14 should be produced after strategic selection and before validation design or full product specification.

Recommended sequence:

1. scope defined
2. T11 active
3. EA and selective T1–T10 completed
4. T12 uncertainty surfaced
5. T13 decision memo selects or advances a vector
6. **T14 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief produced**
7. concept candidates assessed for coherence and constraint fit
8. T15 validation program designed against the chosen concept pathway and assumptions
9. only after validation should fuller product specification proceed

T14 therefore functions as the disciplined bridge between strategy and pre-build experimentation.

---

## 10. Relationship to Other Documents

### Upstream Relationships
T14 depends especially on:

- **T10** for the selected entry vector
- **T13** for the decision logic that authorized movement
- **Ecosystem Analysis** and **T1–T9** for the structural and strategic rationale behind the vector
- **T11** for evidence grounding
- **T12** for assumption visibility and boundary discipline

### Downstream Relationships
T14 directly supports:

- **T15 Validation & Experiment Design Standard** by structuring what exactly will be tested
- implementation-stage product briefs or PRDs by providing a strategically bounded concept frame
- **T19 Learning Capture Memo** by documenting how the concept originated and why
- portfolio comparison or opportunity review when multiple concepts are being generated from different vectors

---

## 11. Core Analytical Questions

The brief should allow a reviewer to answer the following questions quickly:

1. What strategic vector is this concept derived from?
2. Why is that vector attractive in the first place?
3. What force, friction, or leverage point is the concept meant to exploit or resolve?
4. Which participant, segment, interface, or platform is it targeting?
5. What are the viable concept variants that remain faithful to the vector?
6. What value hypothesis does each concept candidate embody?
7. What constraints must shape the concept from the beginning?
8. Which assumptions are embedded in the concept logic?
9. Why does this concept deserve validation before full specification?
10. How would the concept fail if the vector-to-concept translation is wrong?

---

## 12. Required Structure of the Brief

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief should contain the following core sections.

### 12.1 Header
- ecosystem / project name
- brief version
- date
- owner / author
- source vector ID
- status

### 12.2 Source Vector Summary
A concise explanation of the selected vector and why it was chosen.

### 12.3 Conversion Objective
A statement of what the concept generation effort is trying to produce.

### 12.4 Force / Friction Target
The specific ecosystem pressure, participant friction, or leverage point the concept is meant to address.

### 12.5 Target Participant / Segment / Interface
The audience and interaction surface being targeted.

### 12.6 Concept Translation Logic
A disciplined explanation of how the vector becomes a concept candidate.

### 12.7 Concept Candidates
One or more bounded candidate concepts derived from the same vector.

### 12.8 Value Hypotheses
The specific value claims each candidate is making.

### 12.9 Constraint Set
The constraints that must govern concept formation.

### 12.10 Embedded Assumptions and Risks
The most relevant T12 assumptions and failure exposures carried into the concept.

### 12.11 Initial Monetization and Access Logic
A first-pass view of how the concept could capture value and whether it can access the market surface required.

### 12.12 Recommended Validation Direction
A statement of which concept candidate or hypothesis should move into T15.

### 12.13 Supporting References
Pointers to T10, T13, T11, T12, and relevant upstream analytical documents.

---

## 13. Required Data Fields

At minimum, every brief should include the following fields.

### 13.1 Header Fields
- **Brief ID**
- **Ecosystem / project name**
- **Version**
- **Date**
- **Prepared by**
- **Source vector ID**
- **Decision memo ID**
- **Status**

### 13.2 Vector Fields
- **Vector statement**
- **Why selected**
- **Strategic objective supported**
- **Rank or priority**

### 13.3 Targeting Fields
- **Primary participant / segment**
- **Primary interface / platform**
- **Primary friction or leverage point**
- **Trust or access condition**

### 13.4 Concept Fields
- **Concept candidate ID**
- **Concept name / shorthand**
- **Concept form**
- **Core mechanism**
- **Primary value hypothesis**
- **Required behavior change**
- **Delivery surface**
- **Constraint notes**

### 13.5 Governance Fields
- **Critical assumption IDs**
- **Blocking condition IDs**
- **Confidence note**
- **Recommended next validation step**

---

## 14. Source Vector Summary Standard

The brief must begin with a precise description of the selected vector.

This should include:

- the vector itself
- why it outranked alternatives
- the strategic logic underneath it
- what ecosystem condition makes it attractive now
- what forms of value capture it implies

The brief should never assume the reader remembers the T10 logic.
It must restate enough of the vector to make the conversion intelligible.

---

## 15. Conversion Objective Standard

Each T14 brief must state what kind of concept generation is occurring.

Recommended objective categories:

- generate one concept candidate for focused validation
- generate multiple bounded variants from one vector
- test different delivery forms for the same value logic
- compare platform-native versus platform-adjacent concept expressions
- define a minimum viable concept for assumption testing

Without a clear conversion objective, T14 risks becoming unfocused ideation.

---

## 16. Force / Friction Target Standard

The brief must specify the market pressure being targeted.

Recommended categories:

- participant pain or coordination friction
- trust deficit
- timing mismatch
- access bottleneck
- workflow inefficiency
- monetization leakage
- platform gap
- adoption barrier
- decision burden
- capital or attention misallocation

This section is essential because concepts should be shaped by real ecosystem pressure, not by abstract novelty.

---

## 17. Concept Translation Logic Standard

The brief must explicitly explain how the vector becomes a concept.

This requires the author to state:

- what the vector implies must exist or be delivered
- what form the intervention might take
- why that form is coherent with the ecosystem’s structure
- what forms were rejected and why
- why the candidate concept is a faithful expression of the vector rather than a random product idea

This is one of the most important sections of T14.

It is the safeguard against strategic drift.

---

## 18. Concept Candidate Standard

Each concept candidate should be expressed in bounded form.

At minimum, each candidate should define:

- the primary user or actor
- the job or friction being addressed
- the mechanism of value delivery
- the interface or delivery surface
- the core differentiating logic
- the concept form (tool, extension, workflow layer, analytics layer, service wrapper, marketplace app, etc.)
- what is deliberately excluded at this stage

Candidates should be specific enough to validate and compare, but not yet expanded into full product plans.

---

## 19. Value Hypothesis Standard

Each candidate must include one or more explicit value hypotheses.

Recommended fields:

- value delivered to whom
- why the value matters now
- why existing alternatives underperform
- what outcome would cause the target participant to care
- what behavior or adoption signal would indicate the hypothesis may be true

A concept without a clear value hypothesis is not ready for T15.

---

## 20. Constraint Set Standard

T14 must preserve the constraints identified upstream.

Recommended constraint domains:

- platform access constraints
- policy or review constraints
- trust acquisition constraints
- timing constraints
- monetization constraints
- operational complexity constraints
- required integration constraints
- adoption-friction constraints
- evidence or assumption constraints

Constraints should shape the concept from the beginning rather than being discovered too late.

---

## 21. Embedded Assumptions and Risks Standard

The brief must carry forward only the assumptions and risks that materially shape the concept.

Recommended categories:

- demand assumption
- behavior-change assumption
- access assumption
- monetization assumption
- trust assumption
- implementation / delivery assumption
- validation-design risk

These should be drawn from T12, not invented casually inside T14.

---

## 22. Initial Monetization and Access Logic Standard

T14 should include an early but disciplined view of how the concept could capture value.

This should address:

- who pays or what economic event creates value
- whether the concept fits the platform’s monetization pathways
- whether pricing would likely attach to workflow, compliance, convenience, revenue lift, cost reduction, or some other mechanism
- what access path exists to reach the target user or buyer

This section should remain provisional.
T14 is not the final pricing document.

---

## 23. Recommended Validation Direction Standard

The brief must end with a clear recommendation for what should be tested next.

Recommended outputs:

- select one concept candidate for focused validation
- select two candidates for comparative validation
- select one core assumption for direct testing before concept comparison
- defer concept testing until one blocking issue is resolved

T14 should not terminate in conceptual ambiguity.
It must point toward structured next action.

---

## 24. Required Usage Rules

The following rules are mandatory.

### Rule 1 — No concept without vector lineage
Every concept candidate must be explicitly traceable to a selected vector.

### Rule 2 — No freeform ideation drift
T14 is not an invitation to invent unrelated ideas.

### Rule 3 — No constraint stripping
Platform, trust, access, timing, and monetization realities must remain visible.

### Rule 4 — No feature sprawl
The brief must stay at concept level, not backlog level.

### Rule 5 — No validation handoff without explicit hypotheses
A concept must contain stated value and assumption logic before moving into T15.

### Rule 6 — No pretending all variants are equal
The brief should indicate which candidate or pathway appears strongest and why.

### Rule 7 — No conversion without upstream maturity
T14 should not be used to replace unfinished strategic analysis.

---

## 25. Recommended Operating Procedure

### Step 1 — Confirm the selected vector
Verify that T10 / T13 has clearly identified the path being advanced.

### Step 2 — Restate the strategic logic
Capture the core force, friction, and value-capture rationale behind the vector.

### Step 3 — Define the conversion objective
Clarify whether the goal is one candidate, multiple variants, or comparative concept shaping.

### Step 4 — Generate bounded concept candidates
Develop concept options that remain faithful to the vector and constraint set.

### Step 5 — Extract value hypotheses and embedded assumptions
Define what each candidate is really claiming about the market.

### Step 6 — Carry forward critical constraints
Ensure trust, timing, access, platform, and monetization conditions remain visible.

### Step 7 — Recommend a validation pathway
Identify what should move next into T15.

### Step 8 — Archive the conversion logic
Preserve the document as the formal record of how strategy became concept.

---

## 26. Quality Standard / Acceptance Criteria

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief should be considered acceptable only if all of the following are true:

1. The selected vector is clearly identified and explained.
2. Concept candidates are traceable to upstream strategy.
3. The force or friction being targeted is explicit.
4. Concept candidates are bounded and distinct.
5. Value hypotheses are clearly stated.
6. Critical constraints remain visible.
7. Material assumptions and risks are carried forward from T12.
8. The brief provides a clear recommendation for next-step validation.
9. A reviewer can see why the concept exists, not just what it is.

---

## 27. Failure Modes and Misuse Warnings

Common failure modes include:

### 27.1 Ideation masquerading as conversion
If the brief drifts into generic product brainstorming, lineage is lost.

### 27.2 Feature inflation
Adding too much detail too soon makes the concept harder to test and easier to distort.

### 27.3 Strategy amnesia
If the vector rationale is no longer visible, T14 has failed its core function.

### 27.4 Constraint blindness
Ignoring platform, trust, timing, or monetization limits at the concept stage creates downstream waste.

### 27.5 Weak value hypotheses
If the concept cannot clearly state why anyone would care, it is not ready for validation.

### 27.6 False optionality
Producing many variants with no meaningful distinction or ranking creates noise rather than structured choice.

### 27.7 Premature certainty
T14 should shape candidates, not declare product-market fit before testing.

---

## 28. Source and Evidence Expectations

T14 should be anchored in upstream governed artifacts rather than freehand speculation.

At minimum, the brief should reference:

- the source vector and related T10 logic
- the T13 decision basis
- the T12 assumptions that materially shape the concept
- the T11 evidence condition where relevant
- any platform or policy evidence that constrains delivery form

The brief is a translation layer, not a detachment from evidence discipline.

---

## 29. Minimum Brief Template

The following structure should be included in implementation.

## 29.1 Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief Template

### Header
- Brief ID
- Ecosystem / Project
- Version
- Date
- Prepared By
- Source Vector ID
- Decision Memo ID
- Status

### 1. Source Vector Summary
[What vector was selected and why]

### 2. Conversion Objective
[What this conversion effort is trying to produce]

### 3. Force / Friction Target
[What ecosystem pressure or leverage point is being addressed]

### 4. Target Participant / Segment / Interface
[Who and where this concept operates]

### 5. Concept Translation Logic
[How the selected vector becomes one or more concept forms]

### 6. Concept Candidates
| Concept ID | Concept Name | Form | Core Mechanism | Delivery Surface | What Is Deliberately Excluded |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

### 7. Value Hypotheses
| Concept ID | Value Hypothesis | Why It Matters | Expected Signal of Relevance |
|---|---|---|---|

### 8. Constraint Set
| Constraint | Domain | Why It Matters | Effect on Concept Shape |
|---|---|---|---|

| Item ID | Statement | Type | Severity | Why It Matters | Blocking? |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|

### 10. Initial Monetization and Access Logic
[How this concept could reach the market and capture value]

### 11. Recommended Validation Direction
[Which candidate or hypothesis should move to T15]

### 12. Supporting References
- T10
- T13
- T11
- T12
- relevant upstream documents

---

## 30. Relationship to Agentic Research Systems

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief should be designed so that agents can generate disciplined first drafts without dissolving the strategic chain of custody.

This means:

- vector IDs and decision memo IDs should be stable references
- concept candidates should be structured and comparable
- constraint fields should be discrete where practical
- assumptions should link back to T12 IDs
- the recommended validation direction should be explicit enough to hand into T15

An agent may help produce the brief.
The operating system must still enforce fidelity between vector and concept.

---

## 31. Versioning Notes

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief Standard should evolve when any of the following occur:

- repeated conversion work shows that concept drift is still occurring
- T15 reveals that concept candidates are arriving too broad or too vague to validate well
- platform ecosystem work requires more explicit access or compliance translation fields
- monetization logic repeatedly appears too late in the concept process
- learning capture shows that the chosen concept form was not actually faithful to the source vector
- multi-concept comparison requires tighter standardization across briefs

Version updates should record which conversion weakness prompted the revision.

---

## 32. Final Standard Statement

A strategic vector is not yet a product concept.
But a product concept that cannot trace its logic back to a strategic vector is already drifting.

The Vector-to-Concept Conversion Brief exists to preserve strategic fidelity while allowing bounded concept formation.

Without T14, the operating system can identify where to enter.
With T14, it can translate that insight into what may deserve to exist.

---
